Executive Yuan Decides on Partial Reorganization of the Sichuan Provincial Government; Request to the National Government for Posthumous Recognition of Zhang Kairu; Establishment of a Committee for the State Funeral of Former President Li

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan held its 233rd meeting on the morning of the 8th, attended by Wang Zhaoming, Kong Xiangxi, He Yingqin, Chen Shaokuan, Zhu Jiahua, Huang Musong, Chen Shuren, Liu Ruiheng, and others, with President Wang presiding. The following key resolutions were made:

(A) Report Items (omitted)

(B) Appointments and Removals (1) Resolved that the Sichuan Provincial Government be partially reorganized. Gan Jigong, member and concurrently Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, should be relieved of his concurrent position as Director but remain a member. Guo Changming, member and concurrently Director of the Department of Reconstruction, and Yang Quanyu, member and concurrently Director of the Department of Education, should be reassigned and relieved of their respective concurrent positions. Wang Youyong was appointed member and concurrently Director of the Department of Civil Affairs of the Sichuan Provincial Government. Lu Zuofu was appointed member and concurrently Director of the Department of Reconstruction of the Sichuan Provincial Government. Li Weilun was appointed member and concurrently Director of the Department of Education of the Sichuan Provincial Government. (2) Resolved that the resignation of Feng Guorui, Secretary-General of the Qinghai Provincial Government, be approved. The vacancy will be filled by Wang Yingyu. (3) The Ministry of Industry proposed that the resignation of Han Junheng, Director of the Central Factory Inspection Bureau, be approved. The vacancy is to be filled by Zhao Guangting. Please submit the appointment and removal case for approval. The resolution was passed. (4) A letter from the Military Affairs Commission requesting the appointment of Li Jiayu as Commander of the 104th Division of the Army was passed.

(C) Discussion Items (1) The National Government submitted a proposal from Zhu Peide and others on behalf of Zhang Kairu, former Army Commander of the Grand Marshal's Office in Guangdong, who devoted himself to the revolution and endured many hardships, and died of illness on August 1 of this year, requesting posthumous recognition and compensation. It was resolved to request the National Government to issue a posthumous commendation and to posthumously award him the rank of Army General. (2) The Acting Vice Minister of the Interior submitted a report stating that the family of former President Li, Li Shaomou and others, reported that they plan to hold a state funeral for former President Li on November 24 of this year and requested the appointment of personnel to form a committee to handle the state funeral of former President Li. It was resolved to request the National Government to appoint Zhang Qun, Chairman of the Hubei Provincial Government, to organize the Committee for the State Funeral of Former President Li. (3) Minister of Finance Kong and Acting Vice Minister of the Interior Tao reported back on the review and discussion of the Shandong Provincial Government's request to levy additional flood relief surcharges in the counties of the province that were not affected by the disaster. It was resolved that the severity of the Yellow River flood disaster in Shandong Province this time is particularly serious and the situation is special, and it should be submitted to the Central Political Council for special approval. (4) Minister of Education Wang submitted a request for an additional 4,000 yuan in temporary expenditure for the current fiscal year for the Preparatory Office of the National Central Library for the purpose of international exchange of publications, along with a budget estimate for review. The resolution was passed. (5) The Examination Yuan responded that the "Regulations for the Registration of Military Civil Servants" and the "Regulations for the Examination and Determination of Qualifications and Salary Grades for Military Civil Servants Transferring to Ordinary Civil Servants" draft regulations, and the principles of each draft regulation, have been reviewed and are generally appropriate. Please review the main draft, sign it jointly, and submit it to the Central Political Council for approval of the principles and then submit it to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation. The resolution was passed to jointly sign and submit to the Central Political Council. (Central News Agency, 8th)

(Chongqing) The Sichuan Provincial Government will be partially reorganized. Gan Jigong, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, will serve as a full-time member of the Provincial Government. Wang Youyong, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs of Jiangxi, will succeed him. Yang Quanyu, Director of the Department of Education, and Li Weilun, Commissioner of the First District, will switch positions. Lu Zuofu will succeed as Director of the Department of Reconstruction. Guo Changming will be transferred to serve as Commander of the 44th Army Division. The Security Office will also be reorganized. (8th)

(Chengdu) The Departments of Civil Affairs, Education, and Reconstruction are currently preparing for the handover, but the Directors of each department are still responsible as usual. All Directors attended the provincial government meeting on the 8th, and each department is operating as usual. (Central News Agency, 8th)

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Establishes a Headquarters in Yichang; To Be Established on National Day

(Chengdu) Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, in order to suppress the remnant bandits in the border areas of Hunan, Hubei, Sichuan, and Guizhou, has ordered the establishment of a headquarters in Yichang, to be established on National Day. The affairs of the headquarters will be presided over by Chief of Staff Chen Cheng. The staff of the headquarters and all facilities will be transferred from agencies under the Military Affairs Commission. The political facilities in the bandit suppression areas in the border areas of Hunan, Hubei, Sichuan, and Guizhou, in order to expedite processing during the period of bandit suppression, may be directly guided and supervised by the Yichang headquarters. Current Affairs Commentary

What is Expected of Athletes Today

— Bing

The National Games will open on Double Tenth Day. Athletes from all provinces and regions have already gathered in Shanghai, ready to show off their skills. The general public has also shifted their attention away from foreign troubles, floods, and the Italo-Abyssinian conflict, hoping to learn about the grand occasion of this event and hear about the record-breaking performances. Some are even packing their bags and traveling thousands of miles to attend. This shows the importance that the nation places on sports. The fervor is no less than that of other countries. However, in this day and age, the imperialists' aggression towards us is like a fierce wind and torrential rain, and its momentum is increasing. The cry of national crisis has been around for years, but the noose is tightening and there is no sign of relief. Speaking of sports at this time, it should be different from times of peace. This must be noted. What is expected of athletes today is not the selection of a few outstanding heroes to be idols for the general public to admire, but the cultivation of strong bodies for the majority to shoulder the various hardships that lie ahead. Therefore, as athletes, one should not neglect the difference of an inch, a foot, a second, or a fraction of a second, but one should not only compete for the difference of an inch, a foot, a second, or a fraction of a second. As attendees, one should not ignore the competition techniques and athletic postures, but one should not only admire the competition techniques and athletic postures. The same goes for everything else. In itself, there is no such thing as advantages or disadvantages. Only when considering how it is used does it have beauty or ugliness. If those present at the National Games understand this, then even individual track and field competitions will not lose their significance in the present day. And the callisthenics performed by 3,000 primary school students is even more moving. For here one sees the signs of the popularization of physical education and the collectivization of sports. Conversely, if both athletes and spectators are ignorant of this, and only see the National Games as a great opportunity to show off their skills and have a rare good time, then during this time of hardship, spending a lot of money and mobilizing the masses is truly a pointless endeavor. We sincerely hope that it will never come to this.

Speaking of the popularization of physical education and the collectivization of sports, we have endless feelings. Last year, the Ministry of Education surveyed the physical condition of students in colleges and universities across the country. More than 20,000 students were examined, and more than one-third were found to have illnesses. At the same time, in order to improve school hygiene, the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau administered tuberculosis injections to a municipal primary school. More than 800 children were injected, and nearly two-thirds reacted. Regarding secondary school students, Ms. Chen Chuanzhe recently published an article in the Huogong Daily entitled "Save the Middle School Students," stating that secondary school students are burdened by heavy academic workloads and the examination system, and generally suffer from neurasthenia, headaches, and a tendency towards tuberculosis. As far as we can see, we share Ms. Chen's feelings. Young people under the age of twenty have underdeveloped muscles, dry complexions, and cannot sit or stand properly. They seem unable to cope with labor. Observing them at home and on the streets, this is a common sight, almost the rule. Therefore, speaking of the serious problems in the education sector today, the general poor health of students must be the first and foremost, and it cannot be ignored. If this problem is not effectively solved, then everything else is illusory, and there is no glimmer of hope. Today, callisthenics are a regular part of the curriculum in schools, and physiology and hygiene also occupy a considerable amount of lecture time. However, in reality, they are not only useless, but also have the opposite effect. This is because schools treat all training and teaching as routine matters. Callisthenics is not just about having students stretch their arms and legs. It is necessary to examine whether the movements are correct and whether they are persistent. Physiology and hygiene are not just about having students gain knowledge. It is necessary to examine whether their essence is integrated into their daily lives and whether they are practicing what they preach. But if everything is treated as a routine matter, merely ringing the bell to start the exercise and giving lectures on time, what can be achieved? Even worse, schools may ignore the fact that their students are becoming weaker, but they must have one or two athletes who can win at sports meetings to enhance the school's reputation. They may even urge one or two athletes to run and jump every morning and evening, and work hard to prepare for victory, but they are unwilling to pay attention to the daily lives, time allocation, and ability estimates of the general student body, so that they can all have strong bodies. If they go so far as to treat athletic competitions as meaningless, or even as something to be cursed. Now that the National Games are about to open, and we are making these almost disappointing remarks, it is because we fear that the nation will see the grand National Games and forget the general poor health of students. We especially hope that those involved in practical education will take this as the most urgent task at hand. Regarding the physical education of students, it must be as we said, with the aim of cultivating strong bodies for the majority. Under this premise, the popularization and collectivization of callisthenics must be more important than individual competitions, and hygiene facilities must also be related to all training and teaching. This is the right thing to do. All of this must be practiced, so it cannot stop at rules and announcements. It is necessary to measure its effectiveness at all times and in all matters. If this is done for three or five years, and then a survey is conducted, perhaps we can get a report that the physical condition of students is gradually improving. If we get this report, the intense sense of consolation it will evoke in the nation will be no less than witnessing the grand National Games.

Japanese Troops at Gubeikou; Ishii Unit Heads to Chengde

(Beiping) According to sources from Gubeikou, Ishii Nobu, the commander of the Japanese battalion stationed at Gubeikou, led over 300 of his men, including cavalry, infantry, artillery officers, and soldiers, to Chengde on the 6th. Only the Japanese military police, border police, and a garrison unit remained at Gubeikou, numbering no more than 100 men. It is said that there was a civil uprising in Chaoyang County, Chengde Prefecture, and the Japanese troops were sent there to provide assistance. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

(Beiping) The Japanese troops stationed at Malanyu have been traveling by car to Jinzhou since the 2nd of this month in succession. There are now fewer than 50 Japanese troops remaining in the valley. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

Solution to the Outer Pass Telecommunications Issue; Japanese Telegrams to and from Inside and Outside the Pass to be Officially Opened Next Month; Telegram Rates, Settlement Procedures, etc., All Agreed Upon

(Tianjin) The Outer Pass telecommunications issue was discussed on the 7th by Yin Tong and Wang Ruoxi with Takeshita, the chief of the Japanese Shanhaiguan Special Affairs Agency; Fujiwara Yasuaki, Director of Manchuria Postal Services; and Maeda Naotora, Business Manager of the Manchuria Telegraph Company, in Tianjin. It was decided to conclude an agreement on methods of settling Northeast telegram transmission fees, and regulations on Japanese telegram transmission, comprising 19 articles and 5 attachments. Starting on November 1st, the Tianjin and Beiping telegraph bureaus will implement the transmission of Japanese telegrams. Both sides publicly announced the main points of this agreement on the 8th. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

(Tianjin) Takeshita gave a speech in Tianjin on the 8th, saying that the Outer Pass telegram agreement and the acceptance of Japanese telegrams by the Beiping and Tianjin telegraph bureaus are a true expression of friendship between China and Japan, and that the satisfactory resolution of this issue will eliminate at least one obstacle between the peoples of the two countries. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

(Tianjin) Main Points of the Outer Pass Telecommunications Agreement: A. Both parties will settle telegram fees at the end of each month, paying the difference. B. 1. Japanese telegrams are limited to transmission between the South Manchurian Railway's attached territories, the Kwantung Leased Territory, and Harbin, Qiqihar, and Pingzhou. 2. Officially commences on October 1st. 3. Japanese telegrams are charged at five characters per word, with ordinary telegrams at 20 cents per word, code telegrams at 24 cents per word, and news telegrams at 3 cents per word. Urgent telegrams are charged double the ordinary telegram rate. 4. Place names and personal names in Japanese telegrams are calculated as two words. Other procedures follow telegraph regulations. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

(Tianjin) Regarding the restoration of Japanese telegram transmission between inside and outside the Pass, it has been agreed upon by the relevant parties that: A. It will be officially opened on November 1st. The procedures include: 1. Telegram rates are set at 12 cents per Japanese word for telegrams sent to outside the Pass, and 24 cents per code word. 2. Fee settlement will be handled by the Huitong Transfer Bureau in accordance with the established procedures. According to sources in the transportation industry, before the September 18th Incident, Shanghai, Yantai, Qingdao, and the Northeast already had Japanese telegram transmission. Although the Tianjin-Shenyang land line has been restored recently, Japanese has not been opened, and Japanese residents in Tianjin have been forwarding Japanese telegrams to Yuguan for transmission, which has significantly affected the revenue of the Tianjin telegraph bureau. It is necessary to restore transmission to promote business. (Central News Agency, 8th)

High-Ranking Japanese Military Officers Hold Meeting in Tianjin; Discuss Coordination Between Military Departments; Plan to Hold Another Meeting in Shanghai

(Tianjin) An important meeting was held at the residence of the Tianjin Japanese garrison commander on the 7th, attended by Lieutenant General Sakagaki, Deputy Chief of Staff of the Kwantung Army, senior staff officers Tanaka and Hanoka, Chief of Special Affairs Takeshita, Takahashi, the military attache stationed in Beiping, and Japanese military officers Ishii and Nakai from the Tianjin military department. Foreign Embassies Move South; Site Searched for in Beijing; Seven Provisional Measures Formulated for Permanent Lease System

(Nanjing) As foreign embassies move south, the embassy sites are being surveyed by various embassies and consulates in consultation with our government. Seven provisional measures have been formulated for the permanent lease system: 1. Foreign embassies may permanently lease sites within Nanjing City in the name of the embassy to build embassy buildings. 2. Foreign embassies applying to lease land within Nanjing City to build embassy buildings, the location and area of which shall be submitted by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to the Executive Yuan for approval. 3. After the Executive Yuan approves the lease of the embassy site, the rent payable shall be paid in full before the permanent lease certificate is issued. 4. After the foreign embassy has paid all the rent for the embassy site, the Nanjing Municipal Government and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs shall jointly establish permanent lease boundary markers with the foreign embassy. 5. Foreign embassies building embassy buildings shall abide by Chinese laws and regulations and the relevant building regulations of this city. 6. Foreign embassies leasing embassy sites shall not transfer or use them for other revenue or business purposes, except for the office and residence of embassy officials. 7. These measures shall be submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval before implementation. In addition, the Executive Yuan has discussed and stipulated the area of land required for the construction of embassy buildings. The area of embassies is from 40 mu to 80 mu, and the area of legations is from 20 mu to 40 mu. Foreign embassies will follow this standard when surveying sites, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Executive Yuan will jointly deliberate and approve. (Eighth Dispatch)

Ministry of Justice Explains the Doubts About Filling in the Criminal Procedure Review Time Limit Table

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Justice, based on a request from the Henan High Court, explained the doubts about filling in the Criminal Procedure Review Time Limit Table. The ministry's explanation is as follows: The first paragraph of Article 2 of the Criminal Procedure Review Time Limit Rules stipulates that the investigation period shall be calculated from the day after the arrest of the offender. This refers to cases where an offender has been arrested. In cases where the defendant's whereabouts are unknown (Article 220, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law), since no offender has been arrested, the calculation shall naturally begin from the date of receipt of the complaint or accusation document or record. The words "receipt" in the "from receipt to conclusion date" column in the table include the above two situations. As for summoning witnesses, it is a necessary procedure for questioning witnesses, and the time limit should be deducted in accordance with Item 3 of Article 4 of these rules. (Eighth Central News Agency Dispatch)

The Authorities in Peiping Inquire About the Truth of the Vagrants in Da Tan

Reactions to the League of Nations Resolution: Different Responses from Italy and Abyssinia; Abyssinia Continues to Trust that Italy Will Withdraw from the League

(Rome) Italian public opinion, which had believed in the past few days that the League of Nations would certainly agree with Italy's views, feels quite unhappy and shocked to hear that the Executive Council has resolved that Italy has violated the League of Nations Covenant. Many feel that Italy would not withdraw from the League unless expelled, which Mussolini has repeatedly announced. However, there are fears that events will change rapidly, forcing Italy to withdraw from the League. (Reuters, 8th)

(Rome) A foreign ministry spokesman stated today that Italy will soon decide whether to remain a member of the League of Nations, but the future development cannot be predicted until the resolution passed in Geneva is officially announced. General De Bono has not yet reported the number of casualties in the attack on the two cities of Adigrat and Adowa in northern Abyssinia. While the League of Nations is discussing sanctions against Italy, a large-scale demonstration was held by the people of Rome in the Palazzo Venezia. Thousands of people sang patriotic songs to Mussolini and paraded through the streets carrying satirical paintings of the Abyssinian Emperor, shouting slogans such as "Mussolini" and "Adowa." (National Telegram, 7th)

Addis Ababa: Although the Executive Council of the League of Nations has voted to impose sanctions on Italy, the Abyssinian Emperor is still speeding up preparations for war, ready to fight the Italian army to the end. The Emperor has little hope for the League of Nations' power to stop Mussolini. His advisors say that now that Adowa has fallen, French diplomacy can stop the Italian army from advancing, but the Emperor does not believe this. The Emperor stated today, "Abyssinia has not yet begun to fight, but it is imperative to defend all the mountain lines. Abyssinia will meet the enemy with a million soldiers." According to unofficial estimates here, 6,000 Abyssinian civilians have died in the northern route, while the Italian side has lost about 800. (National Telegram, 8th)

Addis Ababa: The Abyssinian Emperor recently issued a declaration to the press, saying that Abyssinia should continue to trust in the wisdom and integrity of the League of Nations. Abyssinia has applied to the League of Nations since December of last year, but the League has delayed processing it, yet Abyssinia still trusts it. Only the Executive Council of the League of Nations can punish unjust acts of aggression. (Havas, 7th)

Addis Ababa: When the Abyssinian Emperor telegraphed the League of Nations requesting it to invoke Article 16 of the Covenant, he strongly stated that the Abyssinian army had obeyed orders and did not resist the Italian army. The claim that the Abyssinian army abandoned Adowa without a fight, in order to prove that Italy was the aggressor in this war before the formal resistance, is emphasized. Officials insist that the reports of Italian planes bombing Abyssinian areas and causing many casualties are greatly exaggerated. For example, in the Balahay area, Italian forces dropped as many as 300 bombs, but only five people were killed and fifteen injured. The Italian war reports and the press claims that many people were killed and injured are not accurate. (National Telegram, 7th)

Italian Embassy in Tianjin Purchases Large Quantities of Coal; Sino-Italian War Affects Tianjin Market

(Tianjin) The Italian Embassy is conducting coal purchases of hundreds of thousands of tons from various mines in Tianjin East, and it is in progress. (Special Telegram, 8th)

(Beiping) According to Tangshan sources, Italy urgently needs coal due to the war with Abyssinia. A special envoy came to Tangshan to negotiate with various coal factories to purchase 10,000 tons of pure lump coal. Negotiations have lasted for two weeks, and the prices have been agreed upon. The contract will be signed soon, the payment will be made, and the goods will be delivered. After signing, the coal factory will transport the coal to Qinhuangdao, where it will be shipped to Italy by Italian vessels. (Special Telegram, 8th)

(Tianjin) Since the start of the Sino-Italian War, the Tianjin financial market has been unstable. Flour, which is mostly imported from Australia, did not arrive last week, causing the price of each 40-jin bag to rise sharply from $2.75 to $3.05, and the price continues to rise. (Special Telegram, 8th)

(Beiping) Italian Ambassador to China, Jacono, has decided to invite leaders from all walks of life in Beijing and their wives to a dance party at the Italian Embassy on the evening of the 15th of this month to celebrate the repeated victories of the Italian army in the Italo-Abyssinian War. (Special Telegram, 8th)

Roosevelt's Actions Support League of Nations Sanctions; US Customs Implements Arms Embargo

(Washington) Although President Roosevelt's arms embargo on Italy and Abyssinia did not prohibit the transportation of raw materials to belligerent countries, he warned that anyone engaged in trade with belligerent countries must bear the risk, which will likely discourage those who transport and sell food, copper, steel, cotton, etc. Moreover, the President's actions are a preliminary guarantee to the League of Nations that if sanctions are imposed on Italy, the United States will not demand the right for American merchant ships to trade with belligerent countries. Observers, after studying the President's order, have stated that member states of the League of Nations can order American ships to stop sailing without angering the United States government. (National Telegram, 7th)

(Washington) US authorities have ordered customs to stop the shipment of arms to Italy and Abyssinia. At the same time, the shipment of military supplies to French Somaliland has also been temporarily suspended, pending further orders. (Reuters, 7th)

(New York) US Coast Guard Commander Hampered has ordered officers under his command to cooperate with customs officials to strictly prohibit the transport of arms to Italy and Abyssinia. Secretary of State Hull told reporters that the US arms embargo on belligerent countries is entirely for the sake of US interests and has not been consulted or cooperated with any country beforehand. (Havas, 7th)

(Washington) The US Chief Tax Officer has ordered customs officials at all ports to detain all arms shipments to Italy and Abyssinia. As for arms shipments to French Somaliland, they will also be temporarily detained, and measures will be determined after receiving orders from superiors. (Havas, 7th)

Britain and America Deny Tacit Agreement on Far East Navy; British Fleet Not Entirely Deployed to Singapore; US Fleet Not Concentrated in Hong Kong

(Washington) Regarding Hong Kong news that the 13th and 14th Destroyer Squadrons of the US Navy will be stationed in Hong Kong, the Navy Department today denied that US warships are concentrating in Hong Kong. The fact that some warships are staying in Hong Kong for a slightly longer time is a normal occurrence every autumn for many years. It is not believed here that there is a tacit agreement between Britain and the United States on naval affairs in the Far East. Italian Strategy Towards Britain: Willing to Participate in Naval Negotiations

(London) The British government had previously notified the United States, Japan, France, and Italy separately to hold naval talks in London in preparation for a naval conference. It has recently been learned that the Italian government has decided to accept the British proposal and participate in the London naval talks. This decision by Italy is generally seen here as an action to ease relations between Britain and Italy. In addition, it is also reported that France has accepted sending naval experts to London to participate in the talks. However, the Japanese government still maintains its original position, that is, Japan's participation in the London Naval Conference should be conditional on all countries first recognizing the principle of naval parity. It is also reported that the Japanese government has proposed that the naval conference should be postponed until next year due to the current tense situation of the Italian-Abyssinian conflict. US Silver Faction Splits; United Front No Longer Exists

(New York) Judging from recent developments, the Congressional silver faction seems to have split into three, each with different interests. According to observers, the united front of the silver faction, which had strong influence, no longer exists. However, there is no organization that openly opposes the silver bill. The first group to go its own way is the faction led by Senator Thomas, whose main goal is to raise the price of silver to $1.29, regardless of other considerations. However, Thomas has now publicly announced that he is abandoning his silver struggle. The second faction consists of congressmen associated with the tobacco industry. This faction previously strongly supported the passage of legislation on silver, but now it acknowledges that the silver policy has severely affected tobacco sales to China and that this policy is not only harmful to the tobacco industry, but also whether it is beneficial to silver producers is questionable. The third faction is led by Senator Pittman. Pittman has managed to use his own special committee to investigate the Treasury Department's silver purchases and has scheduled the first meeting in Salt Lake City on October 12. Although this committee also opposes the Treasury Department, it is more moderate than others. It is expected that the Treasury Department's policies will not change much. (Reuters, 7th)

Telegram from the Huaihai Salt Affairs Inspection Sub-Bureau

Having read the article from Xuzhou dated October 2 in your esteemed newspaper, which states that the Chai Mi North Dyke in the Lihengzhuang area of Donghai County was breached at night by tax police from Guanyun County, causing a flood of water to rush toward the Donghai and Shuyu counties, expanding the disaster area. Upon investigation, a portion of the tax police unit under our jurisdiction was working in Geji and Tangzhuang and other places on the east bank of the Liutang River between September 21 and 29. The unit was withdrawn because the Chai Mi riverbank burst and water poured into the Hai and Guan counties, resulting in futile efforts. Another portion of the unit has been working on the frozen banks of the Yanhai River from September 22 to the present, and there has been no tax police activity in Lihengzhuang, Donghai, breaching the Chai Mi River's north levee to allow water to flow. We request that this information be corrected to protect the reputation of the police. We respectfully submit this telegram for your kind consideration. Huaihai Salt Affairs Inspection Sub-Bureau respectfully.

Public Telegram: Tongshan Suffers from Both Flood and Drought, Awaiting Relief

To Chairman Xu of the Nanjing Relief Committee, Chairman Chen of the Zhenjiang Provincial Government, and Director Zhao, and copied to the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Society, Chinese Jisheng Society, Red Swastika Society, Shen Bao Newspaper, Xinwen Bao Newspaper, and all charitable organizations: Tongshan is located in the northern border of Jiangsu Province, with barren land and poor people. Every time there is a bad year, the young and strong take risks, and the old and weak are left in ditches. Since the flood of the 20th year of the Republic, the rural economy has collapsed, its vitality has been greatly damaged, all industries have declined, and livelihoods are difficult. The Yellow River suddenly changed its course this morning, flooding Tongshan's territory, and the Weishan Lake continued to overflow, causing flooding. Passing through the Jinghe and Bulao Rivers, the flood flowed into the sea. People in the northeast and north villages of Tongshan were displaced, their family properties were destroyed, and the number of livestock swept away was countless. The cries of the old and young are unbearable to hear. Fortunately, our worthy magistrates Commissioner Shao and County Magistrate Wang personally led the local elders, patrolling and blocking the floods day and night, through wind and rain, for two months. Only then was the urban area spared from being submerged. Unexpectedly, since autumn, rainfall has been scarce, and the fields and crops have withered. The southwest villages, which were not affected by the Yellow River flood, have also had no harvest. Some areas are flooded, while others are barren. Both flood and drought have occurred, and the people's lives are unbearable. Now, winter is approaching in an instant. There is no clothing to keep warm, no food to satisfy hunger, and no shelter to protect from wind and rain. We hope that your newspaper will forward this message to all charitable organizations, that they will show great compassion and find ways to provide relief so that we, the survivors, can survive. This association respectfully represents the disaster victims of the entire county in appealing and awaits your orders urgently. The Jiangsu Tongshan Association in Beijing respectfully, with seal.

Guangdong Pirates Burn Ships, Leading to Tragic Robbery

The Sheng Sheng Steamer Encounters Pirates and is Burned Near Shilong, Sinking the Entire Ship and Drowning Over a Hundred Passengers

Guangzhou Correspondent: Transportation between Guangzhou and Shilong Town in Dongguan County has always been convenient. In addition to the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway, there is also waterway access, so no fewer than ten civilian and cargo ships travel between Guangzhou and Shilong every day. Civilian ship tickets are cheaper than train tickets, so many passengers choose the waterway. On the evening of the 1st of this month, the Sheng Sheng electric boat, which runs between Guangzhou and Shilong, was fully loaded with passengers and cargo. It departed from the Wuxianmen Pier on Changdi, Guangzhou, and the journey was calm and peaceful. After midnight, the passengers were asleep. Around 12 o'clock, as the ship was sailing on the Dushu River about twenty miles from Shilong, it was suddenly attacked by more than ten bandits on the shore, who opened fire on the electric boat in an attempt to intercept it. At the same time, undercover bandits on the ship also secretly attacked. Three bandits disguised as passengers fired guns from the cabin to threaten the passengers and set fire to the electric boat. Chaos erupted instantly. The ship's manager, Luo Bao, rushed down from the ship's deck to stop the bandits, but he was outnumbered and was shot in the foot. As the chaos unfolded, bandits on the shore boarded the boat in small boats and began looting. Before long, there were three fires on the ship, with flames reaching the sky. All the passengers on board either died in the fire or drowned in the water. The cries were deafening and unbearable. Only those who were good swimmers were able to escape. Most of the women and children were burned to death or drowned in the water. It is estimated that there were over a hundred passengers and twenty or thirty crew members. Only forty or so people were able to swim ashore or were rescued. The remaining one hundred and twenty or so passengers were buried in the river. After being injured, the ship's manager Luo Bao was rescued by his companions back to Shilong. He immediately reported the incident to the Third Regiment of the Training Division stationed in Shilong. Regiment Commander Chen Ji immediately dispatched a company of soldiers to the scene. By then, the Sheng Sheng had been completely burned and sunk on the beach. The bandits had also fled without a trace. Only floating corpses were seen along the waterway. After this news spread, the Shilong Fushantang Mingshantang and the Guangzhou Convenience Hospital immediately sent specialists to purchase wooden coffins and go to the scene of the incident to retrieve the bodies. On the second day, they retrieved 48 male and female corpses, photographed each one and numbered them, and temporarily placed them in coffins for relatives to claim. Among them were eleven members of the Hongmian Women's Troupe, with only one survivor. On the same day, more than ten floating corpses were recovered from the Huangpu River nearby. Further discoveries were made on the third and fourth days, truly a major tragedy on the river in recent days. The Sheng Sheng is owned by the Yong Tong Yuan Company. In May of this year, it was leased by the Ping An Shipping Company to operate the Guangzhou-Shilong line. The ship is over eighty feet long and can carry two hundred passengers. The engine runs on electric oil to generate power, hence the name "electric boat." Due to the burning, the shipowner suffered losses of forty to fifty thousand yuan, and cargo owners also lost over ten thousand yuan in goods. (October 4)

Zhenjiang

Suzhou Woman Rescued After Attempting Suicide by Drowning

Yuan Yingmei, a woman from Suzhou, is in the prime of her life, with beautiful looks. She graduated from Shanghai Jingcheng Middle School. In February of last year, she met a young man in a Western suit in Shanghai, named Qin Zhi, from Jiangdu. He rented a house in Xihu Fang, Ximen Road. In June of this year, Qin came to Zhenjiang to seek employment in the provincial government because he had been living idly for a long time. However, he disappeared for months without a trace. Yingmei became worried about her livelihood. A few days ago, she came to Zhenjiang from Shanghai and stayed with a relative outside the South Gate. She visited various places for several days, but found no news. She realized that she had been deceived and, in her grief and indignation, she had suicidal thoughts. On the morning of the 8th, she attempted suicide by drowning herself in the Ganlu Harbor East Head. A farmer named Liu Dafu happened to see her and rescued her ashore in time, saving her life. Liu saw that the woman was not ordinary and took her home to get her clothes, so she changed her clothes. After questioning her repeatedly, she told him about the situation. He immediately informed the woman's relatives, who sent her back to her hometown in Suzhou.

Red Cross Relief Supplies Sent to Disaster Areas

In addition, five bags of rice flour, 713 pieces of clothing, and several pairs of shoes and socks have also been collected. All of this was handed over to the Taifeng Shipping Bureau on the 8th to be transported to Jingcheng and then to the disaster area for relief.

International Commercial Telegram - October 8th, Special Commercial Telegram from Reuters -

Gold and Silver

English Gold: Fell again by two pence on the 2nd, to 141 shillings and one pence.

English Silver: The London silver market was sluggish this morning. Spot prices fell 0.125, and futures fell 0.1875, to 29.875 pence. China sold, speculators both bought and sold, and the United States bought. The closing market was stable.

Exchange Rates

US-UK: The London foreign exchange market was quiet this morning. The price of the pound sterling was unchanged. The opening exchange rate for USD-GBP was 4.901875, 0.1875 lower than yesterday's US-UK closing rate. Within the first hour, it rose by 0.125, then fell by 0.125 at noon. It rose to 0.25 at 1 pm and continued to rise to 0.0625 at 2 pm, reaching 4.902125.

UK-France: Opened higher by over four pounds sterling, at 74.35 francs. Within the first hour, it rose by one pound sterling, to 74.38 francs. There were no further changes.

Cotton and Wheat

US Cotton: The New York cotton market opened slightly higher due to rising prices in Liverpool and expectations that the Department of Agriculture's production report would favor the long side. Trading was light as the report was about to be released, but prices continued to rise slightly.

English Wheat: Liverpool wheat market: Prices were slightly lower today. Sentiment is still uncertain. The general pessimistic sentiment internationally appears to be diminishing. At 1 pm, the December futures price was 6 shillings and 5.25 pence, 0.5 pence lower than yesterday's close.

English Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was firm due to expectations that the US government's cotton production estimates would favor the long side. At 1 pm, the January futures price rose by eight pounds sterling, to 6.18.

US Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened lower by about one cent due to easing overseas telegrams and renewed short selling in the market. Subsequent minor declines. Coarse grains fell along with wheat prices.

Rubber

London: The rubber market was firm this morning. January-March futures opened up 0.125 and continued to rise 0.0625 at noon, to 6.1875 pence.

New York: Rubber opened higher, following London, by about 27 pounds sterling. Subsequently prices stabilized. News from Surabaya reported that the Dutch East Indies government had approved the purchase of 20,000 tons of rubber export licenses to prevent the export quantity of rubber planted by natives from exceeding its quota.

Securities

New York: Securities opened steady this morning, with price fluctuations limited to single digits. Risers and fallers were about half and half. After the opening, five stocks plummeted, especially steel stocks and copper stocks, due to President Roosevelt's embargo on arms to Italy and Abyssinia and a slightly more optimistic international sentiment regarding the war. Prices of other securities were relatively stable. The Dow Jones 30 Industrial Average opened at 130.91, up 14 pounds sterling.

Local News

Business Operations Loaning: Changed to Acceptance Bill Fund; Loan Committee Has Approved in Principle; Loan Applications Continue to Be Discussed and Resolved

The Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Review Committee convened a meeting the day before yesterday to review more than 40 loan applications, approving loans exceeding 20,000 yuan. Regarding the 3 million yuan factory operation loan, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce suggested changing it to a fund for promoting acceptance bills. It is heard that the principle has been approved and a meeting will be held soon to discuss implementation. The details are as follows:

Loan Applications Continue to Be Discussed and Resolved

The 14th review meeting of the Loan Committee was held at 4 p.m. on the 7th at the Bank of China. Committee members Cai Zengji, Wang Yansong, Qin Runqing, Bei Songsun (representing Wang), Xi Deluan, Song Ziliang, Zhang Peishen, and others were present. Forty-one applications for small industrial and commercial credit loans were submitted. After reviewing each case, it was decided to approve loans for nine companies, approve half the loan amount for ten companies, approve a reduced portion of the originally requested loan amount for nineteen companies, and reject loan applications from three companies. A total of 25,700 yuan in loans were approved. It is reported that the committee will soon issue notices based on the decisions. Those approved for loans can proceed to sign agreements and collect the funds upon receiving the notice. Those rejected can reclaim the investigation fee of two yuan by presenting their previous receipts. The reasons for the rejections were that one company's business involved manufacturing and selling recreational and entertainment items, which was inconsistent with the purpose of the relief efforts. The other two companies were selling goods that were not domestic products, which was inconsistent with the loan principles. The committee is still accepting applications for small credit loans. Recently, many people have been visiting the committee's office inside the Bank of China on Tianjin Road to obtain articles of association and application forms for loans. However, in accordance with the loan principles, the committee always asks whether they are engaged in domestic goods businesses before issuing the forms. This loan is limited to domestic goods factories and businesses.

Acceptance Bills Approved in Principle

The committee previously planned to allocate 3 million yuan for factory operation loans. It has now been learned that the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce suggested changing the previous plan and allocating this fund to promote acceptance bills, in order to promote this innovative financial initiative for universal circulation. It is heard that the principle has been approved. The detailed measures will be discussed at the next meeting. Furthermore, after this proposal is approved, it must be approved by the credit loan banks and submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval before it can be implemented.

Sharp Increase in Shanghai Goods Exported to the U.S. in the First Nine Months of This Year

The "Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury" reported that the U.S. Consulate General in Shanghai announced statistics today, stating that Shanghai's exports to the United States in the first nine months of this year totaled US$12,274,757. The figure for the same period last year was US$8,578,296, and for the same period in 1933, it was US$7,327,341. However, Shanghai's exports to the Philippines and Hawaii in the first nine months of this year decreased, totaling US$752,414, compared to US$965,104 for the same period last year and US$873,852 for the same period in 1933. The largest increases in Shanghai's exports to the United States in the first nine months of this year were in inedible vegetable products and textiles, which increased sharply from US$383,258 last year to US$2,822,886.

Financial Public Bonds Allocated by the Ministry of Finance: Qian Industry Continues to Repay; Hopes to Safely Navigate the End of the Year

The Ministry of Finance previously allocated 25 million yuan in financial public bonds of the Republic of China in 1935 to rescue the qian industry, establishing the Qian Industry Supervision Committee to oversee everything. It is reported that the Qian Industry Supervision Committee sent a letter to the Qian Industry Association in August, instructing all businesses to repay as much as possible. Up to the second month, the number of repayments from businesses accounts for one-fifth of the total, about 5 million yuan. With the end of the year rapidly approaching, the Ministry of Finance has instructed the Qian Industry Association to continue to accommodate the extension of long-term loans, to rescue industry and commerce and stabilize the market. Therefore, both industry and commerce and the qian industry can safely navigate this month. Regarding the financial public bonds, it has been decided to continue repayment. It is estimated that half can be repaid by the end of this year, i.e., over 12 million yuan. The remaining half will have to be repaid next year.

City Federation Petitions the Municipal Government This Morning: Officially Order Rent Reduction to Aid Relief; Holds a Representative Assembly This Afternoon to Report

The Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Federation believes that the Shanghai market is declining daily, and that disaster victims are eagerly awaiting relief. It has specifically scheduled a representative assembly of district branch representatives at 3 p.m. today to discuss the issue of reducing rents and relieving the market, and at 10 a.m. today, it has sent representatives Chen Jiufeng, Cao Zhigong, Wang Jingdong, Zou Ao Kui, Zhang Xianfang, and others to petition the Shanghai Municipal Government to reduce rents and aid relief to save disaster victims. The details are as follows:

Petition

The federation representatives, Chen Jiufeng, and others, will present the petition to the municipal government this morning. The petition states, "We are submitting this petition to request an official order for the implementation of rent reduction and relief to promote rural relief and revive the city market. The industry and commerce of this city is declining to the extreme. Various industries are struggling to survive, and those declaring bankruptcy and liquidation are coming one after another. Unemployment is constantly expanding, and the lives of ordinary citizens are becoming increasingly impoverished. The reasons for this are: firstly, the bankruptcy of the countryside and the decline in the purchasing power of the vast masses, which has led to the current state of sluggish sales; and secondly, the high cost of rent, which is unbearable and is a source of concern for all citizens and the industrial and commercial sectors. Therefore, to save the situation, it is necessary to make every effort to relieve the countryside, and there is no other way to eliminate the root causes of the disease. Unless rent reduction is implemented swiftly, the current crisis cannot be averted. The association has identified the cause of the problem and is considering remedies. Therefore, there is a suggestion to reduce rents and aid relief, and the fourth executive committee meeting has resolved the following measures: (1) The municipal authorities should be requested to officially order the implementation of a 60% rent reduction; (2) All of the 40% reduction should be used for relief to save disaster areas; (3) The 40% aid relief should be for a period of three months, after which the tenants will enjoy the full benefit of the reduction to ease their burden; (4) The above rent reduction regulations may be revoked by the municipal authorities when the market has reached a considerable level of prosperity. This matter concerns the relief of the countryside, the revival of the city market, and the safety of society. We dare to present the reasons for rent reduction and relief, and have sent representatives Chen Jiufeng, Cao Zhigong, Wang Jingdong, Zou Ao Kui, Zhang Xianfang, and others to petition. We respectfully implore you to consider the difficulties of the times and approve the official implementation. This would be a great blessing. Sincerely presented to Mayor Wu of the Shanghai Municipal Government, Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Federation."

Call for Meeting

The association sent a circular to the representatives of the eighteen district branches attending the general assembly yesterday, stating: "We hereby inform you that a representative assembly will be held at two o'clock sharp in the afternoon of October 9th to discuss rent reduction matters and report on the progress of the petition. This matter is of great importance. We hope that you will take the time to attend and not delay."

Voluntary Registration of Smokers Will End Soon; Police Actively Encourage

The voluntary registration period for smokers organized by the Municipal Public Security Bureau will end in just three weeks. Compulsory registration will be implemented on the first of next month. During this compulsory registration period, self-reporting by smoking civilians will be stopped. Once a civilian is found to be secretly smoking, they will be fined and forced to register. Therefore, the bureau has compiled answers to questions about smoker registration, detailing the significance and implementation of smoker registration. These have been distributed to the public by various branches, so that those who do not fully understand the significance and methods of smoker registration can understand them fully and come forward to register voluntarily as soon as possible. In order to further enhance the effectiveness of the encouragement, the bureau has added investigators to assist the police of various branches in re-investigating smokers and urging them to register since the 5th of this month. This work has been actively implemented and has achieved considerable success. The 15th of this month is the deadline. The number of smokers registered by the bureau has been several hundred per day in recent days.

Reasons for the Delay of the Beijing-Shanghai Night Express Train: Engine of a Freight Train Damaged in Zhengyi

The engine of the 522nd freight train from Maigen Road to Nanjing on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway was suddenly damaged at the 55-kilometer mark between Kunshan Zhengyi stations at about 5 a.m. yesterday, causing the 5th night express train from Beijing to Shanghai the night before to be unable to move forward after arriving at Zhengyi Station. The dispatching department of the railway telegraphed the stationmaster of Zhengyi Station to detach the engine of the 5th night train, drive it to the 55-kilometer mark, push the 522nd freight train to Kunshan Station, and then drive back to Zhengyi to tow the 5th night train to Shanghai. Therefore, it was delayed by two hours and twenty minutes when it arrived in Shanghai. The 301st regular Shanghai-Shanghai train was also delayed by one hour. As for the 522nd freight train, another engine was sent from Shanghai Station to tow it to Beijing.

The JU52 tri-motor aircraft newly ordered by Eurasia Aviation Corporation from Germany officially joined the Shaanxi-Chengdu line on the 25th of last month. Young Aviator Sun Tonggang is Safe in Italy: Some Party Received a Letter from Sun Within a Week

According to the Central News Agency, Sun Tonggang, a well-known young aviator in China, studied at the German National Traffic Aviation School in 1933 and made a 20,000-mile long-distance flight, returning to China from Germany in a self-made aircraft, and then made a national flight, showing a unique color in China's aviation industry. Last year, he went to Italy for further study. However, recently there have been rumors that Sun was practicing aircraft in Italy and fell from a height due to mechanical failure, destroying both the person and the aircraft. This materialization of China's aviation talent was quite shocking for a time. However, yesterday, according to inquiries from a reporter of the Central News Agency to a party closely related to Sun, it was firmly stated that the news was a rumor, because after Sun left the country, they have always been in correspondence. The party told the reporter of the Central News Agency that they had received a letter from Sun within a week, reporting that he was safe on his journey. According to reports, Sun is a famous figure in China's aviation industry. If he had an accident in Italy, foreign telegraph agencies would not have been unaware.

National Government Advisor Millard Resigns: Continues to Manage News Business

According to the "Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury", Dr. Thomas Millard, who has served as an advisor to the National Government since 1930, has now resigned and plans to return to his news business. The doctor was previously a well-known publisher in this city and a correspondent for various American newspapers. He devoted considerable effort to the abolition of consular jurisdiction. In 1931, he published a book entitled "The End of Consular Jurisdiction in China". After the September 18th Incident, he went to Manchuria to investigate. Later, he often traveled to Washington, London, Geneva, and other places. He only returned to China a few weeks ago. Several years before the European War, the doctor founded the English-language "China Press" in Shanghai. During the European War, he was dissatisfied with the British due to his neutral policy, so he lost the management of the newspaper before the United States entered the war. The doctor also founded "Millard's Review" in 1927, which was later sold to Powell and renamed "China Weekly Review". The doctor has served as a correspondent in China for several major American newspapers and has written many books on Chinese issues.

National Federation of Commerce Appeals for Tax Reduction on Hunan Province Brokerage Fees

The National Federation of Commerce yesterday telegraphed the Ministry of Finance stating, "The Hunan brokerage tax is levied at 3% of the commission. Member associations previously received a request from all brokers in Yiyang to forward a petition, pleading for a reduction, otherwise they would cease operations. This matter was forwarded to your ministry last month. Recently, we also received a joint letter from 19 petitioners representing brokers from Xiangtan, including Luo Botao, Liu Songhe representing brokers from Jinshi, He Ru representing brokers from Yueyang, He Zhongjie representing brokers from Yiyang, Liu Zhiqing representing brokers from Changde, Yang Gongxuan representing brokers from Hengyang, etc., stating that since Hunan province changed its taxation method to levy taxes based on commission amount, brokers in various counties deeply feel that the new regulations are cumbersome and difficult to implement, causing widespread discontent. They have petitioned the Hunan Finance Department to revoke the order. Their reasoning is that under the old system of brokerage licenses, the tax levied was relatively light and affordable, with Class A paying 50 yuan annually, Class B 40 yuan, Class C 30 yuan, Class D 20 yuan, and Class E 10 yuan. The new regulations abolish the old tax and completely base it on the commission amount, requiring verification of accounting books to determine the tax base, making the process extremely troublesome. Under this method, commissions, if large, can be taxed hundreds of yuan, and even small commissions will be taxed over one hundred yuan. Compared to the old system, this is an increase of several to over ten or dozens of times. At a time when floods and droughts are frequent, famine is imminent, the rural economy is bankrupt, and the purchasing power of the people is weak, causing commerce to plummet, it is unreasonable to further increase the tax burden on already struggling brokers. Moreover, taxing commissions includes the brokerage firm's employee salaries, rent, and all operating expenses without deduction, making it even more difficult to bear. This tax law is extremely unfair. The Hunan provincial financial authorities disregard the interests of the people, only focusing on increasing tax revenue, thus inciting opposition from brokers in various counties. Although Director Zhang of the Finance Department previously reduced it to 3%, it is still deemed inconvenient. Later, representatives from various county brokers gathered at the Finance Department to petition, and Director Zhang initially agreed to change it, but only reduced the spring and summer taxes by 30%, a ludicrous response. In short, the brokers in various counties, concerned with their own hardships, believe that only reverting to the old taxation method can alleviate their difficulties. Therefore, this petition is not a mere complaint. If the new regulations are implemented, both officials and merchants will suffer. The representatives have always been public-spirited and obedient to orders, but their repeated requests are due to careful consideration of the gains, losses, benefits, and harms, concluding that it severely impacts commerce and the people's livelihood, necessitating relief to maintain the status quo and save what remains. Fearing that the lower sentiments may not reach higher authorities, in addition to dispatching Li Jinfan, a standing committee member of the Xiangtan County Chamber of Commerce, to present the case in person, we have prepared this document to earnestly request your esteemed association to investigate and approve, and promptly forward it to the Ministry of Finance, instructing the Hunan Provincial Government Finance Department to immediately revoke the new taxation method based on commission amount, and revert to the old taxation method based on brokerage licenses to alleviate commercial difficulties and promote prosperity. We also recommend Li Jinfan, a standing committee member of the Xiangtan County Chamber of Commerce, as a representative to petition the association. Therefore, we respectfully telegraph your esteemed ministry to investigate and approve, and promptly instruct the Hunan Provincial Government to revoke the order and revert to the old tax collection method, or reduce the tax rate to alleviate commercial hardships and revive the people's livelihood. This is our earnest plea. Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce of the Republic of China, respectfully. Geng Yin."

Furthermore, the association simultaneously telegraphed He Yunqiao (Jian), Chairman of the Hunan Provincial Government, requesting the revocation of the order to levy taxes based on commission amount to alleviate commercial hardships and revive the people's livelihood.

City Chamber of Commerce Answers Inquiries Regarding Stamp Tax on Receipts, etc.

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce yesterday replied to the Ping Sheng Dun Company, answering inquiries regarding the stamp tax amounts for receipts, delivery orders, invoices, etc. The original letter stated, "We have received your inquiry regarding the stamp duty required for invoices, receipts, etc., and request instructions." The reply is as follows: "(1) Receipts: According to item 2 of the Stamp Tax Rate Table, for receipts of money or goods, each item with an amount or price of three yuan or more requires a stamp of 1 fen, ten yuan or more requires a stamp of 1 fen, ten yuan or more requires a stamp of 2 fen, up to a maximum of 3 fen for amounts over one hundred yuan. (2) Delivery orders: According to the provisions of item 1 of the same table, the stamp tax amount is the same as item 2 for receipts of money or goods. (3) Invoices: According to the provisions of item 2 of the same table, the stamp tax amount is the same as items 1 and 2 for delivery orders and receipts. However, for overdue debt invoices issued during the New Year's holidays, which only list the previous balance for reconciliation purposes, according to Article 3, Section 9 of the Stamp Tax Law, they are exempt from stamp tax. We are replying accordingly, hoping you will take note. Regarding the Stamp Tax Law and its interpretations, our Monthly Bulletin has published a special edition of the New Stamp Tax Law, priced at 1 jiao and 5 fen per copy, available for purchase at our association for your reference."

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce's request to the Ministry of Industry for a thorough investigation of the Xuchang Tobacco Company was reported yesterday. It is now learned that Mr. Shen Weiting, Chairman of the Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Factory Association, believes that many of the statements made in the association's petition are inconsistent with the facts. Yesterday, he sent a letter to the City Chamber of Commerce in his personal capacity, stating, "To Whom It May Concern, I have read the news in the Shen Bao, Shi Shi Xin Bao, and Shang Bao newspapers on the 8th of this month regarding your association's petition to the Ministry of Industry, which states that according to Shen Weiting, Chairman of the Chinese Cigarette Factory Association, the Xuchang Company was organized by Wu Tingsheng with a capital of 100,000 yuan, and the tobacco leaves from the British American Tobacco Company are collected by the company on their behalf. As the crux of the matter lies in whether it is foreign capital, if it is not foreign capital, a written certification should be provided. Shen Weiting believed it was inappropriate and refused to comply. Later, a note was provided stating that the company declares itself to be Chinese capital, but since it was not signed or stamped with the association's seal, it is not an official responsible document, etc. I have found that many of the statements made are inconsistent with the facts. I am now writing to clarify the circumstances to reveal the truth. On the afternoon of the 3rd of this month, Mr. Xue Jianxin visited the association, claiming to have been sent by the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce to investigate the organizational structure and contents of the Xuchang Company. Because Mr. Xue did not present a formal letter of inquiry from the City Chamber of Commerce and did not provide a copy of the original letter from the Shanghai Tobacco Leaf Association, which is different from formal correspondence between legal entities, I immediately stated that I was willing to speak to Mr. Xue in my personal capacity. Subsequently, Mr. Xue, fearing that it would be difficult to remember, specifically requested Mr. Chen Shaohong, the secretary of our association, to record what I said in a written report and then left. The next day, Secretary Chen sealed the report and sent it to Mr. Xue. The report stated that the Xuchang Tobacco Company was established with Chinese capital and registered with the Ministry of Industry. Mr. Wu Tingsheng had indicated to various member cigarette factories that the Xuchang Company's business is to buy and sell tobacco to Chinese and foreign cigarette factories. Any Chinese or foreign cigarette factory can entrust the company to collect tobacco leaves, and the company will be responsible for handling it, charging a commission of 1 to 1.5 fen per yuan.' These were the only remarks I made that day. As the report was recorded by Mr. Chen at Mr. Xue's request, and the conversation was entirely based on personal relations, it was not appropriate to affix the association's seal. Considering the procedure, there should be no impropriety. Fearing that the outside world would misunderstand the truth and cause confusion, I am writing to clarify the situation. I hope you will take note. Yours sincerely, Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce."

Lawyers Association Promotes Formation of Ex-Offender Protection Association

The Shanghai Lawyers Association, to organize an Ex-Offender Protection Association, has scheduled a joint meeting of various city agencies and legal entities for the 13th of this month (Sunday). Yesterday, it sent letters to the City Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, judicial agencies, and other legal entities, stating, "To Whom It May Concern, The organization of an Ex-Offender Protection Association aims to protect those who have completed their sentences, been paroled, or released on bail, enabling them to achieve success. This is not only a crucial measure for the present but also a necessary consideration for criminal policy to prevent recidivism. Various countries in the East and West have long had such organizations, while our country is still in its initial stages. According to Article 2 of the Organizational Outline of the Ex-Offender Protection Association promulgated by the Ministry of Judicial Administration on October 18, 1932, the task of protection cannot be effectively achieved without pooling the strength of multiple organizations. We have scheduled a joint meeting for the 13th of this month (Sunday) at 10:00 AM at our association's headquarters at 572 Beichao Road, Lade Road, inviting various city agencies and legal entities to discuss methods of proceeding. In addition to separate letters, we are hereby informing you, hoping that your esteemed department, government, or association will take note and send a representative to attend and participate in the discussion and jointly devise a plan to benefit society."

Barge Sinks Yesterday in River at Corner of Bund Park; Seven Crewmen Rescued, Cargo Retrieved

Yesterday at around 4:00 PM, a barge being towed by a small steam tug from Yangjiadu to the corner of the Bund Garden capsized. The boat was carrying over 130 bales of cotton. Due to the boat turning too fast, it leaned over and was completely submerged. Fortunately, all seven crew members were rescued by small boats and were unharmed. The cargo was recovered quickly, with no apparent major losses.

China Pencil Factory Begins Operations

China imports millions of dollars worth of pencils every year, but there are few domestic pencil manufacturers. Wu Gengfu, a pencil expert who studied in Japan, recognizing this, returned to China and, with the support of political and business figures such as Yu Qiaqing, Zhang Yongni, Cui Weiwu, Pan Gongzhan, and Ma Yinliang, established the China Pencil Factory, with Zhang Weishi and Wu Gengmei responsible for preparations. This spring, they began installing machinery and building furnaces at 1176 Xiexu Road, Shanghai, using various domestically produced raw materials such as pencil lead, clay, and wood, and employing workers to manufacture pencils. After painstaking research lasting half a year, they successfully produced various brands of black lead pencils, red and blue pencils, and copying pencils, including the "Airplane" and "Ding" brands. The quality of the products is excellent, surpassing that of imported goods. Therefore, the Shanghai Education Bureau, the Literacy Education Committee, various primary and secondary schools, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the Sanbei Shipping Company, the International Telegraph Administration, the Shen Bao newspaper, the Chen Bao newspaper, and the Sixth National Games have all placed orders with the factory. It is reported that in recent months, the factory has been successively inviting people from the local press, financial circles, educational circles, bookstores, and stationery industries to visit, all of whom have praised the factory's perfect equipment, dedicated workforce, orderly layout, and excellent products. The factory officially opened for business on the 8th of this month and welcomes people from all walks of life to visit. It has also prepared 3,000 yuan in discount coupons, packed in one dozen pencils each, to thank customers for their support. The factory has also set up a sales point at the Shen Bao office, shop number 5 in the temporary stores at the National Games, and specially prepared 3,000 dozen pencils as gifts for National Games customers, which is expected to be a great success. The factory's products are also sold in major stationery stores, bookstores, and department stores in the city and other areas.

Chuanjing Hall Publishes Mountain Songs

The Chuanjing Hall Bookstore in the Penglai Market, Ximen, has recently collected old books from Zhejiang and Anhui provinces and obtained a Ming Dynasty woodblock print of "Mountain Songs" by Feng Menglong. The content includes love songs between men and women in the vernacular of the Ming Dynasty. Together with other songs and ballads, there are ten volumes, which have been edited by famous contemporary figures and have prefaces and postscripts. Two images of the original book are attached. It has been printed in a thick volume and is now published. It is an indispensable book for those who study customs and love literature.

Trial Begins for Major Post Office Robbery Case

All Robbers and Armaments Came to Shanghai from Funing

Due to the Complexity of the Case and the Large Number of Perpetrators, the Interrogation Could Not Be Completed Yesterday

—Those Found to Be Unrelated Have Been Released After Investigation—

The North Sichuan Road Post Office was robbed at 9:40 AM on September 9th of this year, resulting in the loss of over 91,000 yuan in silver notes and the fatal shooting of the old office manager Yuan Bingshu and bodyguard Lu Ruilin, and the injury of bodyguard Zhou Yuchen. After rigorous investigation by the police authorities, Detective Shao Jingfan, Detectives Liang Yuliang, Xu Shuiyuan, Zhao Lianbi, and Western Detective Krut, all from the Disiewei Road Police Station, have apprehended the main suspect, the monk Wukong Heshang (named Ji Rentang), and accomplices Qiu Guobin, the woman Wang Chenshi, Ji Chenshi, Chen Qiushi, and suspected accomplices Chen Xiaohongzi, Zhu Xiaomao, Qiu Yushi, Wang Fanshi (all women), Li Yisheng, and ten others.

Confiscated Stolen Money

Over 2,000 yuan was seized. They were handed over to the First Special District Court and the First District Station is under investigation, which is why the news was not previously disclosed. Yesterday morning, the First Special Court held a public hearing. Judge Jiang Shuzi presided over the Third Criminal Court. The police station lawyer Li Zhiyou stated that after investigation by the police station, Chen Xiaohongzi, Zhu Xiaomao, Qiu Yushi, and Wang Fanshi were found to have no direct or indirect involvement in the crime, and therefore, it was requested that their detention be terminated. With the exception of Li Yisheng, whose

Investigation is Not Yet Complete,

It is requested that his detention be extended for another week. Qiu Guobin, Wang Chenshi, Ji Chenshi, and Chen Qiushi are prosecuted according to Article 330 of the Criminal Law. Ji Rentang is prosecuted according to Articles 330 and 332 of the Criminal Law for robbery and murder. First, the circumstances of the post office robbery were described (omitted as it was previously reported in this newspaper). Then, the motives of the perpetrators and the circumstances of the arrest were described. It was stated that initially, the defendants Ji Rentang, Qiu Guobin, Wang Chenshi, Ji Chenshi, and others jointly discussed robbing a certain money shop, but were unable to obtain firearms and abandoned the plan. In August, they again discussed

Robbing the Post Office.

Ji Rentang was responsible for borrowing firearms and accomplices from Funing. Subsequently, several criminals came to Shanghai, bringing four pistols. In total, including Ji Rentang, there were ten people. They learned that the post office would transfer a large sum of money to the savings bureau every Monday morning. At 8:00 AM, they hired a car, number 17671, from the Dalai Motor Company, drove to Qimei Road in Zhabei, forced the driver out of the car, and tied him up. After the robbery, Ji Rentang received 3,500 yuan in silver. Qiu Guobin and Ji Chenshi,

Because They Did Not Go,

Each received only 200 yuan in silver. Because Qiu and others were dissatisfied, Ji Rentang gave Qiu another 25 yuan and Shi 50 yuan. He deposited 1,000 yuan in the Jin Cheng Bank, took 1,000 yuan to Funing, and gave 1,000 yuan to his mistress Wang Chenshi and others to sew into a quilt. On the 21st, they planned to take the Dehe wheel to escape elsewhere. Detectives learned of this and, together with the Public Security Bureau, went to the Dehe wheel and arrested Qiu Guobin and Wang Chenshi. 14 yuan in silver notes were found on Qiu and 317 yuan in silver notes, two silver bracelets, and a gold ring with the name "Little Brother" and a key were found on Wang Chenshi. Then, at 327 Siwen Lane, Xin Zha Road,

Jin Cheng Bank

A certificate of deposit for 1,000 yuan was seized. The money was withdrawn with the gold ring with the name "Little Brother." Later, Ji Chenshi was arrested at No. 2 Pingliang Road and 157 yuan in silver notes were found in her menstrual belt. Chen Qiushi was arrested on Yuezhou Road and 223 yuan in silver notes were seized. Later, together with the Funing Tax Police Corps, Ji Rentang was arrested at the Guanyin Pavilion Temple in the Tianxi Factory in Funing. 15 yuan in silver notes and double-horned notes were seized. After interrogation by the Funing County Government, he fully confessed. The whereabouts of the 1,000 yuan in silver notes sewn into the quilt are unknown and are under investigation. Each defendant had previously confessed in detail to the police station, and the existing confession was presented to the court for review. It was argued that the

Case is Complex

And it is difficult to understand without extensive research. Therefore, it was requested that a special hearing be scheduled. Judge Jiang then interrogated the defendants separately. All the defendants confessed. The interrogation lasted until after 1:00 PM and was not yet completed. It was then announced that the hearing would be adjourned. Chen Xiaohongzi, Zhu Xiaomao, Qiu Yushi, and Wang Fanshi were released. Wang Fanshi was sent by the Shanghai Local Court and should be returned immediately.

Shen Zhenhua, chief of the Old North Gate Police Station, recently found that opium addicts in the area who had been surveyed and repeatedly advised were mostly observing and avoiding registering with the station, which is extremely disrespectful to the law. With the deadline for mandatory registration approaching, he recently

Ordered Police Chief Gao Kui

To lead police officers to Dagjing Road, Luxiangyuan Road, Old Warehouse Street, and other places to arrest over forty opium addicts who refused to register, and bring them to the station and order them to register.
