15th Anniversary of Meiya Silk Factory

China National Goods Production and Sales Cooperative Association

The invention of silk dates back tens of thousands of years in China. Since the opening of the sea, it has occupied the first place in exports, enjoying a reputation in the world market and leading the way for a time.

In recent decades, due to the improvement of silkworm breeds, the advancement of weaving, the brightness of dyeing, and the invention of artificial silk by foreigners, all have made rapid progress, so that Chinese silk has been declining day by day in foreign markets.

In the entire foreign trade war, we are indeed retreating steadily. However, in the history of struggle in these decades, the Chinese silk industry also has many glorious warriors. Meiya Silk Factory is one of the most famous.

Now, Meiya Silk Weaving Factory, with its hundred battles, is holding its 15th anniversary celebration. Recalling the past glory of the Chinese silk industry and admiring the history of Meiya Silk Weaving Factory's right to fight, we sincerely hope that Meiya's efforts will maintain the silk industry and, even more, that Meiya's innovation will lead to the prosperity of national production.

Managing the Economy to Benefit the World

— Lin Sen

A Review of the Factory's 15 Years

— Cai Shengbai

It is difficult to start a business, and it is not easy to maintain it. In the competition of industry and commerce in the 20th century, it is not just about maintaining it. If you don't advance, you retreat. If you don't win, you fail. There is no such thing as success or maintenance. Maintenance means no progress, and no progress means inevitable elimination. Since the establishment of this factory, fifteen years have passed in a flash. Looking back at the initial establishment, the roads were rough, there were only a dozen machines, and only a few kinds of products. Compared with the current achievements, the spring of 1920 is no longer the same. At that time, the machinery was not as good as it is today, the technology was far from as good as it is today, and the methods of promoting sales were far from as good as they are today. However, the needs of the general public for high-quality, exquisite materials were not as high as they are today, and the standard of living was not as high, and there were not as many practitioners, and the competitiveness was weaker, which is also not as good as it is today. Therefore, with the factory's machinery and technology in the past, applied to the past era, it was more than enough to be at ease. It is appropriate that everything went smoothly, the number of machines increased day by day, exports increased day by day, and sales also increased day by day. The foundation of the factory has also gradually been consolidated, from the fifth anniversary to the tenth anniversary, to reach today's fifteenth anniversary. Today is different. Not only are there more and more people engaged in the silk industry, but also talents are emerging in large numbers, and technology is improving day by day. The national material desires and the standard of living are increasing day by day, but their purchasing power, due to years of disasters, famines, wars, and endless trade deficits, has made their purchasing power lower and lower. Therefore, only by making the products more refined and reducing the price step by step can the products be easily sold. How can the cost be reduced? How can the technology be improved? This is the important answer to the present. Therefore, I say that it is not just about maintaining the status quo, but about thinking deeply and seeking progress. I, Shengbai, joined this factory in the spring of 1921, and have been managing everything for fourteen years. Today, I am happy to celebrate the fifteenth anniversary, and I especially feel that the impact of the silk weaving industry on the national economy and the people's livelihood is huge. From mulberry planting and silkworm breeding to silk sales, there are almost 100 million people who depend on it for a living, directly and indirectly. However, the silk weaving industries in Europe, America, and Japan are all above our country, whether in machinery or technology. If we do not catch up quickly, we will undoubtedly fail. If the entire silk weaving industry fails completely, where will the livelihood of these 100 million people be entrusted? The progress of this factory in the past fifteen years, in terms of turnover, although it has increased seventy times, but looking at other practitioners in the domestic industry, those who have not been able to keep pace with this factory and develop together, I feel that the factory's future responsibility is even more serious, and I cannot congratulate myself and be satisfied. The process of technological management and business development of this factory in the past fifteen years can be roughly divided into four periods. The first period was before 1924, when everything was new and initial, and it was all in the early stages, and had not yet reached the stage of advancement. The second period was between 1924 and 1927, when the foundation was established, talents were refined, and gradual progress was planned to seek development. The third period was from 1928 to 1931, when the country was peaceful and the people were safe, so a high-sighted view was taken, and the degree of rapid advancement was almost a thousand miles a day. The fourth period is from 1932 to the present, when times are difficult, the people are poor, and everything is declining. This factory is no exception. It has endured hardships and worked hard day and night, not seeking quick success, and it can barely maintain its position. Looking back at the first period, it was still newly established, and everything was limited by things, and was all of an experimental nature. The founder, Mr. Mo Shangqing, was also running other businesses at the same time, and did not have time to devote all his efforts to this. Therefore, he invited Shengbai to join, reorganized everything, slightly increased capital, added American machinery, stipulated management regulations, and determined business policies, so that the company was on track and began to move forward. However, at that time, the silk weaving industry had not yet made significant progress, and had not broken away from the norms of handicrafts. Therefore, what Shengbai stipulated was only his personal ideal, which he obtained through experience, and he did not dare to say that the blueprint of Europe and America would be suitable for China. He only gradually eliminated the obstacles that were not conducive to the development of the silk weaving industry, in order to lay the foundation for future in-depth research. Moreover, at that time, the domestic economic power had not yet shown signs of exhaustion, and there were not many practitioners. Therefore, although it was in the experimental period, there were few signs of things going against wishes, which eventually led to three or four new products not only being popular in China, but also selling well in Southeast Asia, such as velvet fabric, No. 6 ge, etc., and the business has not declined to this day. These are all extremely memorable achievements in the first period. In the second period, the previous experimental period did not fail, and the excellent results enticed the factory to consider how to expand its business. Therefore, on the one hand, it increased the number of branches, improved technology, and added various high-end products to meet market demand, and prevented the import of high-end silk fabrics, and determined the factory's front-line goal, which was to recover the loss of silk fabrics, and to ensure that domestic silk fabrics and imported silk fabrics stood in an irreconcilable position. Moreover, the factory's organization was a joint-stock enterprise, and the number of branches increased day by day, and the management of personnel had to be carefully considered in order to seek the effect of unified command and increase its effectiveness. Therefore, the General Management Office and the General Distribution Office were established, and each department was subordinate to them, so that they could cooperate and coordinate, and there was no bias or universality. Therefore, the quality of exports has also been improving day by day, and the increase in turnover compared with the first period is six to one. Even in the Jiangsu and Zhejiang sales area alone, compared with the first period, it has increased by more than 30 times.

The beginning of the third period coincided with the success of the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army, the National Government laid its foundation in the capital, and everything was rejuvenated, with a vibrant atmosphere. The factory followed the environment of the times, first thoroughly reforming personnel management, and deeply felt that if political affairs were wise and bright, then all undertakings would also advance. The factory did not dare to close its doors and build cars, so it first established a trial institute, specializing in research and experimentation. On the one hand, it independently invented new products, and on the other hand, it specially dispatched technicians to imitate new European and American products. As a result, the manufacturing factory was able to devote itself to manufacturing, without having to seek invention at the same time, and the types and quantity of products increased even more. At that time, domestic transportation became increasingly convenient due to the government's lack of keenness in construction, and even remote areas were easily connected. Therefore, the factory sent many dedicated personnel to organize exhibition groups, set out to promote, year after year, without regard to cold or heat. The Chinese silk fabrics are as brilliant and radiant as imported ones, and even women and children know it. Since the factory takes the revival of domestic silk fabrics and the recovery of trade deficits as its premise, and at the end of this period, the operators of silkworm businesses in Jiangsu and Zhejiang were failing due to the failure of export sales, and the farmers who planted mulberry trees and raised silkworms were abandoning mulberry trees and planting other crops due to losses, and the factory felt the importance of its responsibility even more. Therefore, it drastically increased production in order to ensure that the silkworms that could not be exported to foreign countries could be consumed in China as much as possible. Fortunately, the factory's efforts to promote sales in the north and south finally succeeded. In 1930, the turnover suddenly increased to more than 5 million yuan. However, the social demand increased sharply, and even though the factory's more than a dozen branches and factories were rushing to produce day and night, they were still worried that the supply would not be enough. They were deeply concerned that the quality might be uneven. The reputation of one factory is small, but the rise and fall of the entire domestic silk fabric industry is related to the national economy and the people's livelihood, so they set up an inspection institute and installed various machines to specialize in pre-inspection of silk and post-inspection of silk. All silk of different qualities is classified and used, so that after the silk is made, each quality meets the required standards. All silk fabrics with slight defects are removed and stored separately, and the reasons for the defects are studied, so that the same mistakes will not be made again. In addition, with the increase in production and the increasing number of personnel, a training institute was established to specialize in training various talents, so that workers and administrative personnel could make the best use of their talents.

The fourth period is that the previous period's rapid progress has achieved great results, and the factory is planning to formulate new plans to seek a major move. However, there were sudden droughts in various places, and the September 18th and January 28th incidents suddenly broke out, leading to the bankruptcy of rural areas, the decline of all industries, and the social economy falling into distress. The purchasing power of the people has also become weaker day by day. Due to the decline in demand for silk, not only is it not easy to expand sales, but also the price has plummeted, which is rare in previous years. The factory has a vast scope and a large number of employees, and cannot afford to hesitate. Therefore, in order to strengthen its strength, in the spring of 1933, the factories were merged and reorganized into a limited company, so that management would be more rigorous and comprehensive. On the one hand, various new products were improved and invented, and on the other hand, various consumptions were saved. Even bamboo heads and wood chips were not abandoned, so that costs could be reduced. Unexpectedly, this year, due to the tight money supply and the floods in various places, it is becoming increasingly difficult to maintain industry and commerce. The factory's colleagues have to agree to endure hardships and work together to fight, and they firmly believe that planning things depends on people, and success does not depend on heaven.

In summary, in the past fifteen years, in terms of the number of machines, the factory has advanced from more than twenty machines to thousands of machines. In terms of the number of people directly employed by the factory, it has advanced from more than fifty people to more than 3,000 people. In terms of products, it has advanced from two or three kinds of ordinary silk fabrics, such as velvet fabric and silk fabric, to velvet, georgette lace, silk yarn, and four-shuttle box three-axis fabrics. In terms of turnover, it has advanced from tens of thousands of yuan to 6 or 7 million yuan. In terms of sales areas, it has advanced from Jiangsu and Zhejiang to various countries around the world. All of these are enough to be the obvious major achievements in the factory's history, which can be described. However, the European and American silk weaving industries are developing a thousand miles a day, and their scale is greater than this. In fact, the factory is still insignificant. Moreover, in recent years, the domestic economy has not been prosperous, and the Yangtze River and Yellow River floods have turned the land into a swamp. Rural areas have gone bankrupt, and their vitality has been greatly damaged. The silkworm industry has fallen by a thousand feet, and the wind and rain have been continuous, with few sunny days. How to maintain the status quo in the future, how to strive for self-improvement, in order to complete the task of recovering trade deficits and helping the domestic silkworm industry, I, Shengbai, am not talented, and I still dare not say that there is a quick solution. However, for fifteen years, the entire staff of this factory has built this foundation together, and they are all willing to work hard, strive to be strong, persevere with perseverance, and be persistent with determination. If we are fortunate enough to be taught by the gentlemen of the country, we will be deeply grateful and eager.

15th Anniversary of Meiya Silk Weaving Factory: Clothing the World

— Respectfully inscribed by Wang Zhaoming

15th Anniversary of Meiya Silk Weaving: Embroidered Splendor

15th Anniversary of Meiya Silk Weaving Factory: Recovering Rights and Interests

Inscriptions for the 15th Anniversary of Meiya Silk Weaving Factory

Shu Brocade Xinxin Wenyan Seeks

Fifteen years of fame throughout Shenzhou

Looking at the indulgent desire to pursue the rising sun

Cautious to the end as if there is no previous affection

Factory Operating History

Our factory was established in the spring of the ninth year of the Republic of China. The initial factory was located in Jiuchengli, Xujiahui Road, French Concession, Shanghai, with only 12 electric looms. In the spring of the tenth year, Mr. Cai Shengbai returned from Lehigh University in the United States with a bachelor's degree in engineering and served as the general manager. He increased capital, added machines, recruited talents, reformed management, and expanded business. Moreover, in view of the old silk weaving machinery in China, in the eleventh year, he first adopted American Otto-type silk winding machines, parallel head machines, thread reeling machines, and Cromwell-style all-iron electric looms to imitate the most fashionable European and American silk crepe, such as velvet fabric, Fangaihua fabric, double crepe, and single crepe, etc. The products were even better than foreign goods, and the sales volume increased sharply as a result. The industry competed to imitate, and the silk weaving industry was renewed. With many looms in our factory and fast delivery, orders from home and abroad came one after another, and the business grew rapidly. In the autumn of the thirteenth year, the second branch was opened on Jiaotong Road, Zhabei. In the spring of the fourteenth year, the Tianlun Meiji branch was established on Xiaoshadu Road. In the fifteenth year, the Meifu Factory was established on Du Shenfu Road. Also, in order to improve the lives of employees, the employees invested in the Meicheng Factory on Xietu Road. At the same time, the Tianlun Meiji General Factory was also established on Xietu Road. In the eighteenth year, the Meili Factory was established on Gonghe Xin Road, Zhabei. Moreover, in view of the fact that the original factories were not able to fully equip themselves, the Mesheng Factory was specially established on Quzhenren Road, Nanshi. The world's most sophisticated machinery was purchased, and the most complete factory buildings were built. All equipment, management, manufacturing, etc., adopted the latest European and American methods. It specializes in weaving various novel and high-end products, such as georgette and Palace, etc. The quantity and quality of the products have been greatly improved, and the sales are even more prosperous. In that year, the Nanxin Factory was established on Xujiahui Road, and the Jiulun Factory was established on Yokohama Road. These are the general outlines of the expansion of the scope and the increase of affiliated silk factories over the years. As for the auxiliary work such as printing, dyeing, and refining, the Meiyi Dyeing and Refining Factory was established in the seventeenth year. All the goods produced by the weaving factories were refined, dyed, and printed by this factory. In the same year, the Meizhang Pattern Making Cooperative was established to specialize in making various pattern plates for the weaving factories. Moreover, the weaving factories have successively increased the number of looms, and the area for expansion is insufficient. Therefore, in the twentieth year, the warp and weft departments of the factories were separated and the Mei Jing Weaving Factory was established to concentrate management and prepare in large quantities. Therefore, the warp and weft weaving, pattern making, dyeing, and refining are all handled by specialized factories, and the division of labor is specialized and refined. The products can be completely standardized, and the credibility of the supply market is increasing.

Our factory was originally a partnership organization, and in the spring of the twenty-second year, it was reorganized into a limited company with an authorized capital of 2.8 million yuan, which was fully paid up at one time. The internal organization and management were greatly reformed after the reorganization. In addition to renaming all the weaving factories as Meiya Branch Factories and numbering them in order, the weaving and dyeing factories were renamed with the Meiya character. The Meizhang Pattern Making Cooperative was renamed Meiya Pattern Making Factory. A general management office was established as the administrative center of the company. The general manager is stationed here to handle affairs. There are six departments under the office, including general affairs, technology, business, finance, procurement, and design, and a secretarial office. Each department is under the command of the general manager and assumes special responsibilities. The factory managers are responsible for the factory affairs and are responsible to the general manager. Moreover, in order to deliberate and develop all the undertakings of the entire company, the general management office convenes various meetings on a regular basis to openly discuss the progress of the undertakings without any isolation or laxity. In addition, three institutes for training, inspection, and experimentation were established. The training institute specializes in the training and guidance of employees. Every employee must undergo strict training before being formally assigned to a position. Other events related to workers' night schools and all sports, entertainment, libraries, and workers' welfare are all handled by the institute. The inspection institute specializes in the inspection of raw materials and finished and semi-finished products. The experimental institute specializes in the research, analysis, and even experimentation of various new fabrics. The establishment of the three institutes is of great benefit to the improvement of personnel and products. The factory organization was completed at this point. All members are working hard in their respective positions, and the work efficiency has been greatly increased. Our factory may be one of the general large factories in China that are magnificent in scale and have the best production for a time.

Our factory currently has 1,200 looms and ships more than 1,000 pieces of goods per day. It is sold in various ports at home and abroad, and the supply is often not enough to meet the demand. There are more than 600 kinds of products, and all kinds of silk fabrics that are popular in all seasons are available. New products are still launched from time to time to meet the needs of the times. Such as velvet, lace yarn, and jacquard georgette, etc., there were no domestic products before. Since our factory first invented and woven them, it has opened a new era in the domestic silk weaving industry. And with the acceleration of production, the rational management, the product cost is reduced, and the selling price is also particularly flexible. The products of our factory are of high quality, low price, and beautiful colors. It is not a fluke that they are popular everywhere and are welcomed by people everywhere.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Xiao Bai)

A flint won't spark without friction, and similarly, the flame of people's lives won't ignite unless they encounter stimulation.

Often, many people don't discover their own "strength" until they're impoverished and have nowhere else to turn. Adversity and tribulation can help them awaken their "self." Hardship and obstacles are like forging one's life into a beautiful hammer and axe. Only failure, only difficulty, only the light struggled for in the darkness can make a person strong and invincible.

Therefore, we shouldn't see all obstacles and tribulations as enemies; on the contrary, we should regard them as benefactors. We can grasp the core of these obstacles and temper our ability to "overcome obstacles."

The words "fate" are untenable; they can never stop us from striving forward!

Burying Oneself in Work Versus Understanding the World

— Wu Yuxiu

Young people should be full of vigor. Never be discouraged by some frustration. Look at the great figures and entrepreneurs of the past and present; who didn't emerge from arduous struggle? When they were unsuccessful, how were they despised and looked down upon? But contempt and disdain only served to strengthen their will and effort.

Society is snobbish. When you achieve success and fame, those who once looked down on you will change their tune and praise you. Therefore, when you are determined to move forward and bury yourself in hard work, let others laugh and curse as they may. Uphold an indomitable spirit and simply work hard. That is the path for today's young people. If you do so, your future will surely be bright.

Often, many people initially intend to pursue a career, but because their ambition is not firm, "every effort is obstructed," and they become half-hearted. Gradually, their aspirations erode and they become "overwhelmed by lethargy," losing enthusiasm for everything they do, just as the saying "understanding the ways of the world" suggests.

This is partly caused by the environment, but partly it is due to one's own abandonment and inertia. By the time "old age arrives" and "time is no more," it is already too late for regrets.

It is evident that young people must avoid the habit of "eat, drink and be merry, for tomorrow we die," and not fail to invigorate themselves. Understand that time does not stand still. When it comes to "being a person," one must clearly recognize the word "being." "Understanding the ways of the world" is a shortcut to deceiving oneself.

Tomorrow is the Double Tenth National Day of the 24th year [of the Republic of China]. I dare to share this speech, “Burying Oneself in Work Versus Understanding the World," with the readers for mutual encouragement.

Chalk

— Yan B.G.

When a teacher enters the classroom to teach, in addition to speaking and gesturing, they rely on chalk to convey words and sentences that cannot be described through speech alone. Therefore, being a teacher is also called a chalk career.

The living expenses of modern elementary school teachers are so meager that it is difficult to maintain a personal life, especially in rural elementary schools, where teachers' living expenses, including food, are only ten yuan per month, which is simply forcing teachers to change careers! Many people are therefore unwilling to eat chalk dust anymore.

Speaking of chalk, in some schools, the principal limits teachers to using only one stick of chalk per class. This is certainly due to the school's financial difficulties, but isn't the principal being a bit too strict?

Not long ago, I taught in a rural area, and several elementary school students asked me for leftover chalk stubs, which was quite troublesome every day. I asked them what they were used for. Some said they were practicing arithmetic, some said they were practicing writing new characters, and some just smiled with pursed lips. I spent a week investigating and discovered that they were using chalk stubs as tools for small gambling. They ground the chalk stubs into squares and used ink to mark "one, two, three, four, five, six," transforming them into good square dice, secretly gambling to win or lose. When they saw a teacher passing by, they quickly crushed the chalk with their palms, so the teacher could not catch them red-handed and did not know what they were doing.

After I discovered this, I sternly warned them that gambling is not something good students should do, and they must adhere to the principle of not gambling! After that, no students asked for chalk stubs anymore.

Achievements of the Past 24 Years!

Four-Year-Old Quits Smoking and Drinking

— Gong

In West Berlin, New Jersey, USA, there is an infant who has just turned four years old, who used to be addicted to smoking and drinking, but has now quit.

This child, named Michael Norman, has loved smoking and drinking since he was three years old. A year ago, Michael took a photo of himself with a large cigar in his mouth, looking very sophisticated, like an adult. This photo was published in the newspaper, and as a result, many letters, like snowflakes, were sent to the Norman home, all from anti-smoking associations and moral reform groups from all over the world.

Michael's grandmother was very moved by these letters, so she started to get him to quit smoking and drinking. According to her proud expression, Michael now only smokes on Sundays, and as for alcohol, he has completely stopped drinking it.

If Michael secretly smokes on another day, then his six-year-old sister, Peach Green, will tell his grandmother, who will immediately force him to throw it away.

Michael is very healthy, with golden curly hair, and his father is a machine worker. His grandmother said that a doctor in New York saw his grandson's addiction in the newspaper and found it very strange, so he came to see the child. As a result, he said that Michael's parts were normal, there were no abnormalities, and he was stronger than other children his age.

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 20: Fighting for Life to See the Beloved Grandson, Embracing Each Other and Weeping, Recalling the Past During a Famine, Sowing Wheat and Inviting Disaster

Shi Lian said, "I just came to the back door once, and it has nothing to do with me if this old lady is sick." Sister-in-law Hu said, "We are not saying anything about your master, we are just asking your master to do a good deed and bring that person out to see her. There is a saying: Saving a life is better than building a seven-story pagoda..." Shi Lian listened to her words, but his eyes were fixed on the old lady. He saw that the old lady's head was slightly tilted and kept swinging forward. Her full head of white hair was blown by the wind and kept falling on her face. Although her eyes were open, the strength of her eyelids was very small, and it could be seen that she was struggling hard, but still could not avoid the tragic sight of them drooping. Shi Lian thought, even if she doesn't die like this, it won't be long. It's best for me to slip away, so he nodded to Sister-in-law Hu and said, "Good, good, I'll tell Master Jia the news and definitely let him release Madam Jia to see her." His words were more powerful than a shot of stimulant for the patient. The old lady immediately said, "Master, if that's the case, you've done a great thing. I'll wait here." Shi Lian felt that things were a bit inconvenient when he heard the dry voice and the intermittent sentences, so he turned around and walked towards Little Western Paradise. Unexpectedly, when he arrived outside Jia Duocai's house, he happened to be entertaining guests, and the sound of their conversation was continuous, coming from inside. He deliberately passed by the window and glanced inside, and saw Yueying lowered her head and huddled in the corner of the room. He thought to himself, if I were to go in and report this unfortunate news at this time, not only would Jia Duocai be unhappy, but the guest would also find me insensitive. (336)

The Drifting Fragrance of the Imperial Incense

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

That evening, knowing that I still had to attend to the Empress Dowager's bath, I respectfully followed her into her bedroom, along with four maids who also entered slowly. At that time, because I did not know what I was supposed to do, I was very flustered, and at first I thought I would have to directly help her take a bath. After a while, I realized that it was the four maids who would directly help her take a bath, and I only needed to stand by and supervise and give pointers. In fact, I had never worked in a bathhouse, so how would I know how to give them such and such pointers? Fortunately, the Empress Dowager did not really want me to take care of her. She liked to take charge of everything, ordering people around haphazardly. How could she relax about this bathing and let the four maids scrub her haphazardly? So in fact, every time we were sent in to "serve" her bath, it would be more accurate to say that we were sent in to "watch" her bath.

First, two eunuchs carried in a large wooden tub, but this tub was definitely not the kind of wooden tub that we ordinary people could see. Although its interior was made of wood, its exterior was wrapped in a thick layer of silver, so it was always very bright and shiny. The tub was already filled with more than half a tub of hot water. In addition to this wooden tub, the eunuchs also brought many clean white towels. At that time, the Empress Dowager was sitting comfortably on a low table. The back of this low table could be removed or installed at any time so that the maids could scrub her back. (433)

Miscellaneous Talk

The Problem of Children Entering Movie Theaters

— Hai

Recently, our education authorities issued an order stating that children under the age of six are not allowed to enter movie theaters. In my opinion, children of this age have not yet developed their intelligence and do not really understand anything. Even if they are shown movies, they will not understand them. Perhaps the reason for not allowing them to enter movie theaters is for the sake of order. In the UK, there are also restrictions on children entering movie theaters, but the age limit is higher. In the UK, some people agree with this, while others disagree. At the time, Jennie Lee, a former member of the House of Lords, published a speech stating that there was no need for such a ban. She said:

"I remember very clearly when the movie theater first came to my village, it was a sensational event. We children eagerly awaited the Saturday matinee. When the day arrived, we took a few pennies, pulled along many younger siblings, and rushed to the movie theater like the wind, so excited that we could hardly breathe. Ordinary seats cost one penny per person, while special seats with velvet cushions cost two pennies per person. There was a loud piano playing familiar melodies, followed by darkness, and the movie began. We shouted with joy at the sight. I still remember a car on the screen getting closer and closer, bigger and bigger, scaring a fat old lady in the front row, who jumped up, fearing that she would be hit by the car. But we children, hearing her screams, applauded and cheered, finding it very amusing.

"However, while we children welcomed the movie theater, our parents strongly opposed it and forbade us from going to such a bad place again. Now, twenty years later, when I think of the past, I cannot help but ask myself, should we allow children to go to movie theaters?

"According to my past experience, the answer is, of course, we should allow them to go. Because movie theaters are most capable of satisfying children's curiosity? Movie theaters are simply like the magic carpet in "One Thousand and One Nights," taking us to many places, meeting people from different countries, observing rural life, and studying the endless variety of machines. The movies also have funny people who make us laugh; despicable villains who make our blood boil; and the suffering in Mary Pickford's films, which make us sad and tearful, and we want to learn to comb our hair into curls like hers. What we children especially welcome are those cowboys and Native Americans in Western movies, riding horses back and forth. After watching the movies, we would run home as if riding horses, thinking we were cowboys and Native Americans, and all the games we played were often copied from the screen.

"Then those who oppose movie theaters will say, 'Precisely because of this, children should not be allowed to go to movie theaters. The cowboys and Native Americans have largely disappeared from the screen, replaced by the hooligans and thugs of Chicago and New York.' Children who watch these movies get a bad impression. Those children who are good at imitating, when they go home, will imitate the behavior of hooligans and thugs, treating it as a game. Isn't this very dangerous?

"Children's games are just games, and they will not necessarily learn the behavior of hooligans and thugs and commit crimes that violate the law. If it is for the sake of preventing trouble before it happens, then local officials and education authorities should not allow such films to be shown on the movie theater screen. Why should they deprive children of the right to watch movies because of this?

"Although many of the events in movies are based on fantasy, there are also many that depict the realities of human life. For example, early American films mostly portrayed the adventurous history of the development of the West, so cowboys and Native Americans were often active there. Modern American films often portray the criminal history of gangs in the city. These films can all be said to depict real life. What is most shameful is that the British film industry often imitates the bad aspects of Hollywood to produce films. Anyone with a sense of responsibility should organize and throw these films into the vast ocean, not only not allowing children to watch them, but even adults should not watch them.

"In short, if anyone wants to absolutely prohibit children from watching movies, I will oppose it to the end. You must know that in a few years, they will have to enter society. Whether the films are good or bad, they can give them a taste of life. When they enter society and live that real life, they can use everything they have seen in the films as reference material.

"If we want to purify this evil world, this filthy society, then adults should take responsibility and not do evil, so as not to be filmed and have a bad influence on children. This is the fundamental solution. As for prohibiting children from watching movies, that would be like abandoning eating for fear of choking."

Then, due to poor Liverpool telegrams, Southern sellers dumped their holdings, and the weather was good, so market prices continued to soften. However, [Business] Continent and the Far East all bought in. Later, Liverpool banks sold overseas and took positions here. Therefore, the opening price plunged by a huge three to four fen. Due to the weak confidence in the forward months, the prices for February and March fell by a huge one jiao compared to the previous day's initial opening price. This kind of violent rise and fall was caused by international price trends. In addition, long positions were being liquidated, so more than 800,000 bales were traded in half a day. By the afternoon opening, the market atmosphere turned slightly stable. Because the bullish sentiment of outside parties increased, large amounts were pulled in, and the market was supported. After this, if foreign wheat can be approached, there will be no excessive price increase.

Free Talk

"Ideal Love" and "Practical Love"

—Xin Ren

Many "young men and women" who cannot get rid of the "scholar's aura" originally wanted to "bury" their responsibilities for the "era" in a vigorous way. These people know that now is no longer the time to devote themselves to "falling in love" and "cherishing spring," but to do some actions and careers with "social significance."

This motivation is worth admiring. However, many young men and women who have a "recognition" begin to be excited and frenzied when they step on the road of social action, then become anxious and unbearable, and finally become passive and decadent. At this time, they want to shout but have no courage and talent, and they cannot help but hesitate.

This is indeed a major problem among today's "young men and women." And this problem cannot find a complete answer in some "youth education" like training.

However, more than half a century ago, Feodor Dostoevsky exposed this problem with "painful cruelty." In the second book and fourth section of the great novel "The Brothers Karamazov," a high monk Zosima, who should now be honored as "Living Buddha," said that a doctor once confessed to him in this way:

"I love mankind, but there is one thing that surprises me. This is nothing else, that the deeper I love mankind in general, the less I love individual human beings. In imagination, the matter of contributing to mankind has reached almost strange ideas, as if one can carry a cross for mankind at any necessary opportunity; but on the contrary, I cannot spend two days with anyone in a house together. This is known from experience. As soon as someone is close to me, his personality immediately oppresses my own self-esteem and freedom. So I can even hate those with outstanding personalities in just one day and night. Some eat for too long, and some have a cold and constantly sniff, which makes me hate. In short, as soon as people come into contact with me, I immediately become his enemy. Conversely, the deeper the hatred for individual human beings, the more enthusiastic the love for all mankind follows."

This doctor's confession is not just a sharp scalpel toward himself, or simply toward "us." High Monk Zosima (who is of course Dostoevsky's "gramophone") explained that this is "ideal love" as opposed to "practical love." He said:

"Practical love is almost terrifyingly difficult compared to ideal love! Ideal love hopes for rapid success and wants people to see it. In fact, there are some extreme people who want to make it successful without delay, like the ones shown on the stage, so that everyone admires it; even if they lose their lives because of it, they will not hesitate. However, when it comes to practical love, there is nothing else but labor and patience!"

The so-called "labor and patience" here should be meaningful only when one leaves the "position of slave philosophy." This remark of Dostoevsky is similar to the words in the "New Testament" "Matthew's Gospel" Chapter 23, verses 3-7 of the "Bible."

"...They can say but cannot do. They bind heavy burdens that are hard to bear, and lay them on people's shoulders, but they themselves are not willing to move a finger. They do everything to be seen by people, and make their phylacteries broad and their tassels long. They love to sit in the best seats at feasts and in the highest places in synagogues, and love people to greet them in the marketplaces and to call them Rabbi, Rabbi."

Of course, this type (the "scholar" is the "scholar" of today—and the "Pharisee") mentioned in the "Bible" is different from the type mentioned earlier, but it cannot be ignored. Conveniently, here one can perhaps catch a glimpse of Dostoevsky's "spiritual connection" with the "Bible"; on the other hand, one can also know that although the "Bible" has always been revised and embellished, it still protects many immortal and brilliant lights to this day.

The shift of the center of gravity of love from the personal love of "falling in love" and "cherishing spring" to "the love of all mankind" is a progressive process. History has used countless lives and blood to awaken general "young men and women" from their "pink dreams." But once awake, the drowsiness is still there, and the darkness is long in front of you. Here the problem becomes a problem.

We may as well listen to the precepts of that high monk Zosima: "The most important thing is to avoid hypocrisy, all kinds of hypocrisy, especially hypocrisy to oneself. Observe your own hypocrisy, every hour—no, every minute, to discover it!"

The so-called "observing one's own hypocrisy" does not mean that we should leave everyone and spend the whole day hiding in the house staring at our own noses. Without examining all our actions in behaviors related to social mankind, we cannot obtain "self-knowledge" and "self-salvation."

The contradiction between "ideal love" and "practical love" is manifested in the duality of thought and behavior. The characters in Dostoevsky's works are all suffering in the contradiction of this duality. This duality is certainly the inheritance of their environment, but it is not an irreconcilable defect. If Dostoevsky also knew that "God" is ourselves, then he would not give such illusory and almost desperate hopes to his many protagonists who are in the "underground room" and suffering from "crime and punishment."

Among us "scholars," generally, the more those who speak, the more they have this kind of "duality of love." But—"Why do you see the splinter in your brother's eye, but do not notice the log in your own eye? How can you say to your brother, 'Let me take the splinter out of your eye,' when there is a log in your own eye? You hypocrite, first take the log out of your own eye, and then you will see clearly to take the splinter out of your brother's eye." ("New Testament" "Matthew's Gospel" Chapter 7, verses 3-5.)

Let the Death Knell Sound! (Prose Poem)

—Mu Zhi

Let the death knell sound—

The radio on the street plays jazz, flirtatious tunes, and vulgar Cantonese music with squeaks and crashes: that is the curse of the desperate, the delirium of those with popular fever, the exhausted groans after wild beasts mate, the carnival night before suicide... Listen, the dying giant is singing his own requiem!

Let the death knell sound—

The rhythmic sound of doorplates! The pulse of this metropolis! Breaking through the silence of the deep night. Main streets, alleys, here, there, all echoing this sharp and monotonous magic music. The cursed people gradually return to silence from shouting, laughing, and scolding! Deathly silence! They stare at each other with vengeful eyes, staring blankly at the dice of fate, holding their breath and listening to the drops of life's blood dripping away. What they occasionally [win] is money, but what they lose is their limited and boring lives. Listen, the dying giant is wielding the hoe and shovel himself, building his own tomb!

Let the death knell sound—

Here, the name of Buddha is murmured, and there, the scriptures are sung loudly: here, serpent spells are written, and there, solemn Dharma assemblies are held. Sorcerers fly with covetous salivation, and good men and women kneel and offer their blood and flesh. Ghosts and foxes are exposed, and wandering souls and zombies play on the streets. Good, good! The giant in the sickbed has heard the last prayers and is being exorcised!

Let the death knell sound—

Preachers put on a stern face and [recite] the doctrines on paper, and priests diligently advise others to do good; the delirium does not forget the glory of the past, and ancestral fake antiques are caressed in the hands of bankrupt households. Listen, the dying giant is dictating his will in the last moment of his life! Isn't the death knell still ringing?

Market

— Zigan

The auction houses, noticed and frequented by a segment of savvy individuals.

This is a "market," a "market" for those who have money left over after covering their living expenses. It resembles the ancient tradition of alternating-day markets, but separated by a chasm of money. It's like comparing a farmer's rough cigarette for relieving fatigue to a fine cigar held in a white hand while reclining on a sofa.

Advertisements are the cornerstone of credibility for merchants, tirelessly broadcasting auction dates daily in black and white – excellent opportunities for everyone to strike it rich.

Outside the large glass windows, shrewd eyes linger, hoping to discover something worthwhile. If you ask the managers, they will gladly tell you with boastful exaggeration. This inspires comforting dreams for some customers in the days leading up to the auction.

If the weather is clear, the auction house fills with people early in the morning. Aside from some easily inspected wooden furniture, every eye is eager to examine each item from the first to the last – miscellaneous household items, clothing of fine material but slightly worn, exquisite and ingenious toys, bundles of assorted medical books…

Speculation, caressing, hesitation—

A greasy-faced attendant patrols, keeping an eye out for pickpockets, and also answers customers' questions, such as: how the bidding increases today, and if there are any new items. The most experienced simply use their eyesight; these are secondhand dealers whose eyes and minds consult, grander than the ragtag collectors on the street, but they also hold their small drumsticks behind their ears with an air of examination: careful! Occasionally, people in different trades greet each other, revealing solemnity before the battle.

On schedule, the auctioneer walks onto the table—a temporary command post. A smile vanishes, and the entire room falls silent.

The handler checks the catalog and calls out the numbers, while assistants busily hold up the items being called, exaggerating slightly at the corners of their mouths, occasionally turning back to question the busy handler, providing some verification.

Listening to the handler's explanation of the items, hearts in the room begin to race, deciding whether to take aim, bid, increase the price.

Initially, it's some odds and ends, like bottles and jars, ironing implements, kerosene stoves, spittoons... These small items instead stir hesitation among the buyers. The handler bustles about, adding detailed notes, even:

"Medical spittoon, old brand, no blemishes..."

"Foreign porcelain toilet, old Swedish temper—" Unable to resist Chinglish: "Closet Sweden made; made by Sweden."

The audience bursts into laughter.

However, the price also increases, rising from a few cents to two or three dollars.

Upper-class Chinese quietly watch, and foreigners sit comfortably in high places listening attentively. The most excited are the "experts," their eyes more focused than a cat watching a mouse, seizing their target item, watching the price rise and fall.

As space gradually clears in front of the table, the "experts" climb up, holding cigarette butts, using their black hats to support their open chests, sweat on their foreheads condensing some wit and calculation, their gaze shifting from the target item to the rivals, or perhaps rivals, also eyeing the same target. Everyone exchanges malicious smiles, indicating their expertise, with an air of "a fight to the death."

Spraying saliva, they vigorously increase the price, the one with the fuller pockets emerges victorious.

Abuses occur; those slightly more familiar with the process know that if the high price exceeds the true value, the rivalry stirs envy among the customers, and eventually, the one who pays the most is not an expert, but an amateur fool.

Here, too, are old book buyers, harboring great expectations for the whole bundle of foreign books, even though the letters are as unfamiliar to them as if from another world, they are willing to take them over for a closer look when the price is right, not afraid of the joke of looking at the book pages upside down.

Buyers who specifically search for one or two books have to give up because some books are useless to them. The booksellers reveal smug smiles on their faces.

Until the final wooden furniture is called, people calm down. The percentage of those items needed by each person is not large, and those who have gained nothing slip out, leaving some victors to wait for their spoils.

Those who leave have bitter faces, smiling faces, and embarrassing grins—

Dawn

— Meiyu

A swiftly falling meteor,

Shatters the walls of darkness.

The whip of darkness,

Draws forth the brilliant sun.

A piercing whistle,

Is the cheer of tens of millions.

Tattered hemp shoes,

Step onto brand new soil.

The Honored Old Woman (5)

— Written by Ema Shū, Translated by Ren Jun

The Russo-Japanese War erupted. Yongzao's division immediately mobilized for the front. The old cook woman ran around, showing everyone the letter Yongzao sent when he departed. The gist of the letter was: "From now on, I will be a soldier fighting for the country. Even if I die, I will never die in disgrace. I will not die before I have done my best to defeat the enemies of justice and humanity. Therefore, Mother, please do not grieve and worry too much. Just pray that your son can fight bravely and honorably on the battlefield." It was completely filled with the strong spirit and courage worthy of a soldier. The old woman showed it to everyone, asking them to read it to her again and again. And each time, she sighed deeply several times, as if overcome with emotion; then, with tears in her eyes, she spoke, lavishing the greatest praise on her capable son.

Everywhere, people talked about the war. Old men and children alike discussed nothing but the war. Then, the Japanese army won battle after battle, both at sea and on land. People felt exhilarated and fanatical. They had all become mad militarists. And the towns and villages were filled with cheers of "Banzai!"

The old cook woman was naturally no exception. Wherever she was, if two or three people gathered to talk about the war, she would put down her work and crane her neck to listen. Moreover, she tried desperately to learn about the war's situation and progress. Before long, she had memorized the names of various places in Manchuria, the names of the division commanders, and military terms; and she began to talk about the war herself. However, there were simply too many unfamiliar words, and she often made strange mistakes, which was inevitable. For example, she pronounced Urazhsky as "Ulazhiluosibei," landmine as "landmine-ya," Lushun as "Luoshunkou," and Niuzhuang as "Jiuzhuang"... etc. For her, there was only one place name that she could easily remember after hearing it once, and that was Nanshan. According to her, the pronunciation was the same as the two words "difficult birth."

"What, the Russian devils, fifty thousand, one hundred thousand, what's the big deal. My son alone is enough to deal with them. They probably don't know that the Japanese army has my son Yongzao in it."

She said this with a fierce expression. After saying it, she suddenly laughed out loud.

The attack on Lushun began. The division from our area also participated. Thus, in the peaceful countryside, notices of deaths and injuries in battle began to arrive.

"Today we received a notice of the death of so-and-so from such-and-such street!"

"I heard that so-and-so was seriously injured!"

"Honorable death, honorable injury!"

Remembering the Past

— Ouyang Fanha

In the eyes of most intellectuals, the past seems like a beautiful fairyland. If they hear an old woman in the countryside say that each generation is worse than the last, they will certainly think that the old woman is nothing more than a stubborn old person, but they never even dream that, in essence, they are just like the old woman in longing for the beautiful dreams of the past. The reason they consider the past to be so good is actually entirely due to their disappointment with the future and their disgust with the present.

There are originally two types of people who are dissatisfied with the status quo. One type is dissatisfied with the status quo and therefore reminisces about the past, feeling that the more ancient the better, childhood is better than adolescence, adolescence is better than youth, youth is better than middle age; or elementary school is better than middle school, middle school is better than university, university is better than entering society. They are also filled with grief and indignation at the unsatisfactory status quo, as if a Qing dynasty comprador, seeing his son wearing a Western suit, becomes so angry that he pounds his chest and stamps his feet, and thus thinks of the glorious days of hanging a queue behind his head in years past, and cannot help but secretly shed tears. They are hopeless about the future, only feeling that they are heading towards the abyss day by day; Freud once pulled a face to explain that mankind has a spiritual reflection of missing the life in the mother's womb, transforming into a beautiful mountain spring landscape or grassland water color reverting to the dream. This theory, when quoted here, completely loses its solemnity and becomes a mocking of people.

The other type of person who is dissatisfied with the status quo is not like this. They hate the present, but they know that a better future than the present will come. They hold infinite hope for this future, and they develop beautiful longing. Here they find comfort, or they single-mindedly indulge in the realization of this beautiful dream of the future and have no time to even consider the past. However, they are by no means unrecallful of the past, but their method of recollection is completely different. They are never recollecting the past for the sake of admiring the past or reminiscing about the past, thinking that the past is good to linger on and go back to. No, if they recall the past, they must have a purpose consciousness, and this purpose consciousness is very clear and sharply defined, that is, to analyze the past, distinguish between the various different existences of the past, and thereby learn from the past experiences that can be used in the present. This is almost close to scientific research. Apart from this reason, they have no time to go back to the past. They are busy enough pursuing the future to grasp the present.

In the eyes of the former, all the ugly elements of the past are completely excluded, leaving only a mesmerizing, multicolored scene. Using this mesmerizing scene, they treat it as wine for themselves to drink, indulging in it to pass away their increasingly decadent leisure life.

In the eyes of the latter, the ugliness and beauty of the past coexist simultaneously. It is merely a segment of the human process or their own process. When they take a glance at this segment, they must ask how much recognition of the past has been lost in spending the time now to benefit the future? Following the emergence of the bourgeoisie, the classics of Greece and Rome were all recalled and recognized, and this recall was entirely for the sake of the bright and brilliant future of classicism. After the French Revolution, the bourgeoisies of various countries, in their ascendant times, recalled all the reforms after the French Revolution and copied them in the same way, and at that time they were full of a thriving youthful spirit. They never wasted half a moment on these pasts, and after they had finished studying those pasts from all aspects, they returned to their own studios with no feeling at all, as if they were at peace.

But the aristocrats of the French Restoration were different. Looking at the manor that had changed its shape, the peasants who had changed their character, recalling the former Louis era, thinking of the Bourbon dynasty, they spent their remaining lives washing their faces with tears every day. They treated the past as a food, and only the past was the only kingdom where their souls could escape. This situation, reflected in the romantic longing for the Middle Ages, is very similar to that of a severed arm.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

The Consumption of Superstitious Goods

— Mengruo

Eliminating superstition in China is still not possible today. First, because superstition is originally an inherited thought, passed down from a distant ancient time, which cannot be changed in a single day. Second, because the power of superstition is deeply rooted in the general public, which also cannot be eradicated in a single day. However, superstition is ultimately a harmful thing, and its existence poses a great obstacle to the development of the nation. Therefore, although superstitious thoughts are not easily eradicated in a single day, it is necessary to find ways to prevent their spread and gradually eliminate them.

Here, I will temporarily set aside the spiritual and behavioral influences of superstition and only look at the economic losses, which are quite alarming. According to the survey conducted by the Fujian Provincial Government, the consumption of superstitious goods in the entire province is more than 5.5 million yuan per year. If the consumption of superstitious goods in one province reaches more than 5.5 million yuan per year, this number is not small. If we add up all the provinces in the country, the national consumption of superstitious goods must be 100 million yuan per year (at least 70 or 80 million yuan). This is an even more enormous figure. In China, where people's livelihoods are declining, most citizens are still struggling to maintain their daily food and clothing. Adding this significant burden every year, their difficult situation can be imagined. This issue deserves attention.

However, the Fujian Provincial Government has no way to reduce this unnecessary loss for the people and is now going to impose a special tax on superstitious goods. Whether this measure is appropriate is worthy of examination. According to reports, Fujian Province has passed a proposal submitted by the Financial Design Committee to impose a special tax on superstitious goods. Based on the consumption of superstitious goods in the province, which is more than 5.5 million yuan per year, a tax of 30% will generate about 1.1 million yuan per year. By implementing this special tax on superstitious goods, the Fujian Provincial Government can increase its tax revenue by 1.1 million yuan per year, which is a huge income. But where will this 1.1 million yuan in taxes come from? Directly from the merchants who manufacture superstitious goods, and indirectly from the people who consume superstitious goods. In this way, the consumption of superstitious goods in Fujian Province, which was originally more than 5.5 million yuan per year, will now increase by 1.1 million yuan, becoming more than 6.6 million yuan. This is a heavier burden for the people.

Or someone might say that since superstition should be eliminated, imposing a special tax on superstitious goods is a method of prohibiting through taxation, which is not necessarily blameworthy. I think this statement is not necessarily correct. Using the method of prohibiting through taxation to eliminate superstition is like using the method of prohibiting through taxation to eradicate opium. This can only make superstition more rampant. If we are truly determined to eliminate superstition, we must change people's thinking through the power of education on the one hand and prohibit the manufacture of superstitious goods so that people have no way to use them on the other hand. If we can do this, even if superstition cannot be eliminated in a single day, it is not impossible to gradually eliminate it.

Page 22

A Night at the Inn

— Yixia

The weather is over ninety degrees, and even the finest twigs on the treetops do not sway slightly. On a rectangular low table, a kerosene lamp is burning. In order to make the flame particularly bright, the glass cover is smoked black by the kerosene fumes, so the room is shrouded in an extra layer of dimness. Several outdated newspapers are spread out on the table. Apart from a few large characters in the headlines, it is difficult to recognize anything else clearly.

It has been half a year since I left my hometown. When I came out, I was wearing a leather coat. Now everything has changed. These days, unexpected changes can happen to you anytime, anywhere. On the journey, I heard news of floods everywhere, from the Yangtze River all the way to the Yellow River, from the Yellow River all the way to the Grand Canal and the Huai River. Everywhere there is news of water, everywhere there are statistics of dead people, everywhere there are advertisements for disaster relief. But you have no way of knowing the accurate news. Everyone is shaking their heads, everyone is sighing. In the city, everyone is busy. Everyone can tell you how terrible the flood is and how tragic the disaster is. It seems that the entire China has already sunk. Although the water has not yet reached my feet, has not yet reached your feet, everyone is panicking, everyone is immersed in the torrent of recession.

However, you have no way of knowing the news you want to know. You can find statistics in the newspaper, you know how high the water is, how much farmland is flooded, how many millions of losses there are. You can also find pictures in illustrated magazines, seeing the crowds of disaster victims. But you still haven't found the news you want to know.

Friends, my hometown has already been buried under the flood, this is what I know, and you also know. However, these days, there are too many changes, too fast. I don't want to know this general news, I want to know more, more specific.

I know my familiar hometown. There is a blue high sky, yellow-white land, winding paths. When I left it, the grass was withering, spread out on the ground, and wheat seedlings were spreading at the foot of the mountains, it was a beautiful, magnificent mountain village.

Now it is early autumn, it should be when the green grass decorates the entire hometown. The leaves of the white poplars are shining, twinkling on the hillside, the persimmons are red, and the jujubes are ripe. Especially the Guandi Temple in the poplar forest at the foot of the mountain. Those are all familiar to us.

I know the stockaded village, I know the earthen walls of the stockaded village, I know the oily green grass that regrows on the earthen walls every year. I also know the seeds that this grass bears every year in early autumn; those are lovely little things, bright red.

The leaves of the white poplar trees are about to turn yellow-red with the arrival of autumn. The red walls of the Guandi Temple, the red seeds of the grass, the red leaves of the white poplars, are the autumn that children are intoxicated with. Especially the harvest time, it is the time of rural songs all over the fields.

There is also our home, the people in our home, and the neighbors.

But now it has changed, everything has changed quickly.

We know that water is flooding everywhere, from the Yangtze River to the Yellow River. Everyone is panicking, everyone is shaking their heads and sighing. In the city, everyone is busy. Busy with disaster relief, sighing that there are too many changes these days, panicking about this recessionary torrent.

It is already early autumn, and the weather is so hot. The glass cover of the kerosene lamp is even dimmer. The newspaper brought from the city three days ago, although it is old, is still the only fresh news.

Under the dim light of the kerosene lamp, recognizing each word one by one, regardless of the sweat all over my body, regardless of the greedy mosquitoes, turning the newspaper over and over again.

How is my hometown? The leaves of the white poplars, the walls of the Guandi Temple, and the seeds of the grass. And the home, our home, family members, and neighbors.

The newspaper says this… it says fields, houses, disaster victims, and various statistics of losses.

Jiupanzi (Continued)

— Youqi

This dropped a huge bomb among us. We understood why he hadn't spoken and why the coolies were silent.

—What to do? This became our collective demand. "Biting the bit and running fast" was certainly a good method, but what if it didn't work out? So, we were at a loss.

I don't know why, but suddenly I thought of the outlaw heroes in old novels. The appearance of them appearing on stage reminded me of burly figures with angry eyes, thick eyebrows, thin-soled boots, and reminded me of a loud shout stopping the way, steel knives rising and heads in different places, and even reminded me of roars like thunder shaking the mountains... I tried my best to bring up all the appearances I could imagine in my brain. Why did I want to think like this? I don't know, I just felt that it had to be like this.

It is said that when a person's mood is uneasy, their nervous senses are very sharp. This was tested today. A burst of horse bells rolled in from the other side of the mountain, and my heart would shake. The leaves on the trees made a few more noises, and even passers-by looked at us more, which could arouse our animosity, making us think of another situation.

The Dasha Ditch passed unconsciously, and Jiupanzi stood tightly in front of us—

Squeezing my heart, cold sweat broke out on my head. I quietly lightened my pace as I walked. Old Huang and Old Wei held the weapons they had brought tightly in their hands, looking at the sky. The sun was covered by dark clouds, and the time was approaching six o'clock.

The sky seemed to be deliberately opposing us. At the critical moment, it was terrifyingly dark. There were some things wriggling in the distance, which could not be guessed or seen clearly.

Stepping onto the top of Jiupanzi Mountain, I don't know why, but the coolies in front, led by the coolie leader, shouted their jargon, like a long snake, on the sheep intestine mountain road hidden by trees, which had a special flavor.

What is the reason? Don't worry about it. We know Lao Zhang's wit. Good, let's sing loudly too!

So, we sang out-of-tune mountain songs, stretching our throats, and the lingering sound lingered in the mountains.

Passing through a sloping hillside and reaching the top of the mountain, we looked around. The mountains joined hands and formed a circle, and in the middle became a large deep valley. No matter which side you came up from, you would never realize what was going on in the deep valley until you reached the top. Call for help? Don't even think about it. In fact, there is no way to find your trace at all. Unless you are foolish, you will never achieve that unfortunate result.

The sky was strangely dim. It looked like it would rain tonight. People waiting in the mountains were not surprised by this. In the place where miasma condenses, the weather is unreliable. The stream and the whistling wind, although they can increase the natural interest, we have no time to appreciate them.

——Ah? How lucky we should be! After going down the mountain, I took a deep breath.

The time pointed to six o'clock. Coolie leader Zhang ran over from the front with a flushed face and said——

——Oops, it's too late. We can't make it to the distant place. We have to rest at Guanyin Bridge today.

——Walk faster! Hey, stay at Guanyin Bridge!

It is easy to go down the mountain but difficult to climb up. In this way, we fell into the station before the lights were lit. From the rumors of the people in the station, we knew that this place was a dangerous place. We knew that single travelers often had to sacrifice themselves, and we also knew that before two or three o'clock, some people had suffered unfortunate encounters here.

——Don't go to look around in the nearby places! Be more careful at night! Lao Zhang repeatedly told us.

When we had dinner, there were still many people who came to watch. They still had towels wrapped around their heads, but in our eyes, we always felt that they were harboring evil intentions and were full of killing.

It was night, and everything around was silent. Listening to the whistling wind and the chirping insects, our hearts were surrounded by unstable air, uneasy.

——When will it be dawn? These are hard times!
