Shen Bao Local Supplement - Automobile Weekly

Discussing the Special Features of Three-Wheeled Automobiles

— Yu

Ever since the automobile came into being, in the minds of most people, it has been assumed that if an automobile is to be built, then the four wheels on the car are a matter of course. They cannot be increased, nor can they be decreased. However, this kind of thinking is not necessarily the case in the eyes of another group of uniquely ingenious people. They feel that the existing 5,000,000 automobile users are somewhat too traditional in their thinking. Therefore, in recent years, after painstaking research, they have discovered that three wheels are best for an automobile. Not only is this their ideal, but there are also several automobile manufacturing engineers who specialize in designing three-wheeled automobiles. Regardless of whether these three-wheeled automobiles can become popular on the market, they always feel that this kind of automobile has its own indelible advantages.

The attention paid to three-wheeled automobiles is still a fact of a very short period of time. Therefore, the number of these vehicles can be said to be extremely small. According to current investigations, there are about ten or more different styles that have been discovered in Europe. As for China, it can be said that there are no such three-wheeled automobiles yet. All there are are three-wheeled motorized bicycles. These motorized bicycles are mostly used for transporting light items.

Among the few three-wheeled passenger cars in the United States, there is recently a type of Bucksminster Fuller's "Dymaxion." It can be said to include all the advantages of three-wheeled automobiles. The most noteworthy are: (1) Excellent streamline. (2) Ease of operation. (3) Reduced weight. This car is a large automobile, and the car compartment is very spacious, but its weight is only 3,000 pounds. It is powered by a Ford engine and can travel 100 miles per hour. It can park on the side of the road with only a gap as long as its body. The driver can start the front wheel and turn its rear wheel. If parked in a tight and narrow space, the driver can first drive the front end of the car in, turn the rear wheel to an 80-degree angle, and then start the engine to turn the rear end of the car in. The two spacious passenger seats are located in front of the engine. Speaking of the arrangement of its wheels, it is like a three-wheeled bicycle traveling backward, and its operation is similar to that of a three-wheeled bicycle. Some people say that the convenience of this car is something they have never seen before.

Why is people's interest in three-wheeled automobiles gradually increasing and rising? It may be helpful to briefly explain the reasons here. If we go back to the past, the roads were still paved entirely with dirt. When the car drove on the ground, it left two ruts. Therefore, the wheels of the car had to be manufactured according to the ruts. The gauge of the horse-drawn vehicles in the northern United States was about 56.5 inches, and in the southern United States, it was 60 inches. Therefore, early automobiles had to be fitted with a size between the two, depending on the needs of the buyer. Although there are still some dirt roads left now, most of the roads have been converted to hard surfaces. Whether the wheels of the car can match the ruts is certainly not a problem.

Another advantage of three-wheeled automobiles is streamlining. The term "streamline" has now been overused by everyone. Strictly speaking, the so-called streamline of general automobiles today only achieves its likeness in form and some superficial aspects. However, some people still believe that even if an automobile is made to be truly streamlined, its benefits are not entirely certain. Now let's talk about the shape of a quasi-streamlined type. If we dissect a typical fish into two halves, then the upper half becomes a streamlined shape. The widest beam is near the front, and the tail end is tapered. There should be no protrusions in the appearance to ensure its smoothness. The wheels must be wrapped up. Headlights, mudguards, etc., must also be integrated into the same form as the car body. If this shape conforms to the streamlined type, then this automobile must be three-wheeled. Because there is no room for two wheels at the tail. The reduction of wind noise, fuel economy, and the increase in acceleration are all special features of streamlined cars. As for the increase in speed, it goes without saying.

Speaking of the appearance of the car body, most people think that the three-wheeled car is more beautiful than the four-wheeled car. There is even a group of people who say that apart from three-wheeled cars, no automobile can match its beautified posture. Regarding the issue of weight reduction, everyone has their own opinion. Some people say that the weight required for a three-wheeled automobile is less than half of that of a common automobile. Whether this figure is accurate or not is not stated here for the time being. Just based on ordinary knowledge, the weight of a three-wheeled automobile is not more than three-quarters of that of a four-wheeled car. The car body of a three-wheeled car can be manufactured using a conical metal sheet. This metal sheet is light and strong, similar to the skeleton of a single-wing airplane. Therefore, the weight of a three-wheeled automobile is certainly not excessively heavy.

The manufacturing cost of three-wheeled automobiles is said to be greatly reduced compared to ordinary automobiles. Not only because of its light weight, but also because the body configuration is simple, the cost is also greatly reduced. Various inlays, etc., can be manufactured on inexpensive turning machines, unlike the currently popular automobiles, which must be manufactured on die-casting heavy pressure and other machines, which are very expensive. Regarding important manufacturing issues such as engine style, position, weight distribution, and power management, it is not possible to solve them all at once. However, those engineers who are researching the manufacture of three-wheeled automobiles believe that the center of gravity, if it is a car with a wheelbase of 125 inches, must be between 20 to 30 inches behind the front axle, then the safety of a three-wheeled automobile during driving can be increased compared to a four-wheeled car. Because the steering of this car only uses one wheel, all the common front-end problems can be eliminated. The position of the engine can be changed according to different weight distributions. The allocation of seats also depends on the engine position.

The picture on the right shows a strong Ford truck traveling in the desert near Gansu. In the hinterland of northwestern China, where deserts are intertwined, mountains rise and fall, or rivers freeze, the Ford truck has many amazing records in transportation under such circumstances.

History of the Development of Diesel Engines for Automobiles (1)

— Zhu Yisheng

The reason why the original diesel engine is so eager to be popularized in Europe and the United States is fourfold: (1) Diesel engines can burn heavy oil, which is cheaper. The ratio of heavy oil to ordinary gasoline is almost one to three. (2) It is not equipped with a carburetor and is not affected by cold weather and freezing. (3) Cumbersome and heavy spark plugs, storage batteries, and motors are eliminated. (4) Heavy oil is not as easy to burn as light gasoline. It adds a lot of security in terms of safety.

Just a few months ago, a Cummins six-cylinder diesel sports car started from New York, crossed the new continent to Old Saint in California. The journey was three thousand seven hundred and seventy-four miles. However, the heavy oil consumed by the Qin was worth only 7.63 U.S. dollars, equivalent to about 16 silver dollars in our country. It burns only about four cents worth of heavy oil per 100 miles of travel. This can be described as a new record for oil use in the automobile industry.

The world's machine engineers have long held great hope for the effectiveness of diesel engines more than ten years ago. The reason for the delay in development until today is that coal production was high and prices were low at that time, and water engines were easy to manufacture. There was no need for much change and saving. Today, however, commercial warfare is becoming more and more fierce, especially under the cloud of recession. It is necessary to strive for economy in consumption. So, the diesel engine is still there. Today, everything from streamlined trains, automobiles, postal ships, and airplanes is being improved and competing to install diesel engines. Other facilities such as hydroelectric power plants, tillers, and power for the entire factory are gradually adopting diesel engines. At present, my country's machine factories can also imitate and manufacture them for small industries such as water pumping, rice milling, and cotton ginning. However, due to the low metallurgy, the crude machine furniture, and the disregard of arithmetic, my country's products have not been able to compete with imported products for a day. Not to mention the engines used for automobiles and airplanes.

Last year, in the United States alone, the total horsepower of diesel engines manufactured by various machine factories was as high as 750,000 horsepower. It is estimated that it can be doubled this year. All factories that used to manufacture gasoline engines are now opening special departments to study the manufacture of diesel engines. In the past twelve months, various improvements have made rapid progress, creating a new record in the world's power industry.

The reason why diesel engines are more economical than other types of engines is due to their great efficiency. For example, a few months ago, a large European machine factory built a large engine with 5,500 horsepower. The test results showed that its efficiency was 41% (that is to say, for example, if 100 pounds of heavy oil is added, only 41 pounds is actually effective). This is much higher than 21% for water turbines, 10% for gasoline engines, and 6% for train water engines.

Since diesel currency has so many advantages, why not popularize it earlier? The reasons have been briefly described in the previous paragraph. Now I will extend the discussion from the various problems in manufacturing and operation.

Ford Driving Comfort in Hot Weather

The refinement of the new Ford V-8 car makes summer driving exceptionally comfortable. The reason for this is that the Ford car's ventilation system is a major factor. In addition, there are individually controlled adjustable screens, wide-diaphragm cowl ventilators, and window ventilation equipment. When the weather is scorching, the windows, screens, and cowl ventilators can all be opened to allow a large amount of air to enter the car. In ordinary weather, the cowl ventilator can be opened first. If the weather turns cold at night, or there is a drizzle, the cowl ventilator can be closed, and the window ventilation gap can be opened to allow the stale air in the car to slowly escape through this gap, and then fresh air can be let in without the intrusion of drafts.

There is also a new "deflector" type engine ventilation setting, which can improve the cold operation of the engine even in the most difficult summer conditions. All the airflow from the engine fan face is sucked into the holes, goes down through a conduit into the crankcase, then flows upward into the valve chamber, and then exits through the vent holes, along with the water quality and other steam, so that the engine oil can be cooled and prevented from deteriorating during high-speed summer operation.

The design of the V-8 engine ensures that each row of four cylinders has a separate set of water jackets. This ensures rapid and accurate water flow. Each cylinder is completely surrounded by a water jacket, extending its entire length. Therefore, even under severe operating conditions, "hot spots" and cylinder distortion can be prevented.

In order to protect the car from the effects of heat, the new car model is equipped with external ribs to increase its heat radiation area and strength. In this way, even frequent braking can avoid the "weakening" of the car brakes, because frequent stopping can cause the brake drums to expand, thereby reducing the effectiveness of the car brakes.

Car drivers pay attention to using as little force as possible when driving. In this regard, the 1935 Ford V-8 is a real help because its transmission box operates more softly and efficiently. This new transmission basin utilizes centrifugal force to make meshing more definite, and greatly reduces the pedal pressure required when disengaging. If you want the paint of your car to shine brightly in the summer, it is very important to clean it often. However, Ford cars are easier to satisfy this wish because they use a new type of baked enamel finish. This finish does not change even under the strong light of the summer sun. It can be as bright as new with just a rinse.

(2) County Roads Completed in Each District

Nanning District: Nanning-Yongning 25 (li), Funan 80, Yongchun 218, Long'an 100, Hengxian 175, Wuming 500, Binyang 100, Shanglin 120, Nawei 115, Longshan 150, Du'an 170, totaling 1753 li.

Zhennan District: Longzhou 185, Pingxiang 73, Yangli 40, Zuoxian 30, Jingxi 44, Shangjin 150, Sile 150, Wancheng 147, Qianjie 110, totaling 794 li.

Liujiang District: Liuzhou 160, Liucheng 80, Sanjiang 150, Laibin 90, Xiangxian 160, Yishan 65, Si'en 85, Nandan 35, Rongxian 90, Yishan 50, Qianjiang 70, Luorong 30, totaling 1061 li.

Guilin District: Guilin 500, Yongshou 60, Yongfu 27, Yining 87, Quanxian 180, Huiyang 90, Pingle 28, Gongcheng 90, Fuchuan 105, Mengshan 55, Zhongdu 50, Liujiang 20, Yu'an 70, Hexian 80, totaling 994 li.

Cangwu District: Xindu 35, Guiping 90, Guixian 110, Wuxuan 70, Yulin 140, Bobai 90, Zhuangliu 60, Luchuan 200, Xingye 50, Tengxian 100, totaling 9XX (missing digit) li.

Tannan District: Baise 50, Tianbao 234, Pingzhi 67, totaling 351 li.

New trunk lines: 6443 li. County roads: 5898 li. Total: 12341 li.

As for the toll collection methods for each road, large passenger vehicles are charged 2.2 jiao of silver per 10 li, small cars are charged 2.6 jiao, and freight transport of general merchandise is charged 1.2 jiao of silver per 100 jin per 10 li, while agricultural products are halved. This regulation is somewhat expensive, but because gasoline is imported from overseas and the price is high, current fares cannot be reduced. The Road Bureau has recently used kerosene oil residue and alcohol charcoal gas to replace gasoline, and the test results are good. However, kerosene oil residue is still imported. In order to avoid the outflow of money, special attention is paid to burning charcoal. After future promotion, the fares can be greatly reduced. In addition, automobiles are only used on provincial and county roads, and cannot travel on village roads. Agricultural transportation is still difficult to popularize. The Road Bureau has been modifying various ox carts, horse carts, and rickshaws in recent months in order to pass through village roads, so that provincial, county, and village roads are connected to each other to facilitate the transportation in rural areas and promote the sale of production.
